Correcting the Genealogy of Sahib al-Wiqayah
Biographical entry with genealogical correction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to correctly identify the author of al-Wiqayah and distinguish between the two scholars known as Sadr al-Shari'ah.

Core Idea
The author of al-Wiqayah is Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud, not his brother — a common genealogical error corrected by reliable sources.

In Hanafi biographical literature, the identity of the author of al-Wiqayah is sometimes confused. Several later scholars mistakenly attributed the work to Burhan al-Din Mahmud, the brother of Taj al-Shari'ah. This passage, from a commentary on Rasm al-Mufti, carefully examines the lineage and clarifies the correct genealogy. Understanding this correction is important for accurate citation in Hanafi fiqh and usul studies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main figure
The passage first introduces Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad as the author of al-Wiqayah. Note his full name and lineage.
Taj al-Shari'ah is the grandfather of the famous commentator of al-Wiqayah.
2
Trace the disputed genealogy
Several sources (al-Qahistani, Kashf) claim the author is Burhan al-Din Mahmud, brother of Taj al-Shari'ah. Mark this as the error.
This would make the author the uncle of the correct person.
3
Understand the author's verification
The passage author declares he has verified the matter using reliable declarations in his own commentary. The correct lineage is that Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud wrote al-Wiqayah for his grandson, the younger Sadr al-Shari'ah.
The fa'idah clarifies the two Sadr al-Shari'ahs: elder (Ahmad) and younger (Ubayd Allah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب الوقاية : هو الإمام تاج الشريعة محمود بن صدر الشريعة أحمد ابن عبيد الله جمال الدين العبادي المحبوبي البخاري. أخذ العلم عن أبيه صدر الشريعة الأكبر أحمد عن أبيه ، كان عالماً ،فاضلا ،تحریراً ،کاملا محققا، مدققا . ألف كتاب الوقاية الذي انتخبه من الهداية، صنّفه لأجل ابن ابنه صدر الشريعة عبيد الله بن مسعود ابن تاج الشريعة، كذا في أعلام الأخيار ، وفيه أيضا : عبيد الله صدر الشريعة ابن مسعود ابن تاج الشريعة صاحب شرح الوقاية، حافظ قوانين الشرع، ملخص الأصل والفرع عالم المعقول والمنقول، فقيه، أصولي، محدث، مفسر، أخذ العلم عن جده تاج الشريعة محمود، وكان ذا عناية بتقييد نفائس جده وجمع فوائده، شرح الوقاية من تصانيف جده تاج الشريعة ثم اختصره وسماه "النقاية . وألف في الأصول متنا سمّاه التنقيح " ثم صنّف شرحا سماه " التوضيح " . مات سنة ٧٤٧هـ، ومرقد والديه وأولاده وأجداد والديه في شرع آباد "بخارى"، وأما جده (أبو أبيه) تاج الشريعة، وأبو والدته برهان الدين، فإنهما ماتا في "الكرمان " ، ودفنا فيه كذا ذكره عبد الباقي الخطيب بالمدينة المنورة. وفى مدينة العلوم : من شروح الهداية نهاية الكفاية" لتاج الشريعة وهو ،محمود كان عالماً ، ،فاضلا ،كاملا، وله مختصر الهداية المسمّى بـ" الوقاية " . أقول : هذا كله نص على أن مصنّف الوقاية هو شارح الهداية تاج الشريعة، وإن اسمه محمود ابن صدر الشريعة الأكبر، وإنه جد صدر الشريعة شارح الوقاية من قبل أبيه، والمشهور أن مصنف "الوقاية " جد فاسد لشارح الوقاية، وبه صرح القهستاني في جامع الرموز حيث ذكر : أن شارح الوقاية صدر الشريعة عبيد الله بن مسعود بن تاج الشريعة عمر ابن صدر الشريعة وإن صاحب الوقاية، برهان الشريعة محمود بن صدر الشريعة أخو تاج الشريعة وكذا ذكره صاحب الكشف : "أن الوقاية للإمام برهان الدين محمود بن صدر الشريعة صنّفه لأجل ابن بنته صدر الشريعة". والله أعلم بحقيقة الحال، وقد حققت الأمر بتصريحات الثقاة في مقدمة شرحي لشرح الوقاية، فلتطالع .

فائدة : صدر الشريعة اشتهر به اثنان يوصف أحدهما بصدر الشريعة الأكبر، وصدر الشريعة الأول، وهو أحمد بن جمال الدين عبيد الله المحبوبي، وهو والد تاج الشريعة" ، وثانيهما يوصف بصدر الشريعة الأصغر، وصدر الشريعة الثاني : وهو شارح الوقاية عبيد الله بن مسعود بن تاج الشريعة محمود بن صدر الشريعة الأكبر، كذا في "الفوائد البهية " .
Sahib al-Wiqayah: He is Imam Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad ibn Ubayd Allah Jamal al-Din al-Abbadi al-Mahbubi al-Bukhari. He acquired knowledge from his father Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar Ahmad from his father. He was a scholar, virtuous, editor, perfect, verifier, accurate. He authored the book al-Wiqayah, which he selected from al-Hidayah. He compiled it for the sake of his grandson Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah. Thus in A'lam al-Akhyar, and in it also: Ubayd Allah Sadr al-Shari'ah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah, author of the commentary on al-Wiqayah, keeper of the laws of the Shari'ah, summarizer of the original and the branch, scholar of the rational and transmitted, jurist, usuli, hadith scholar, exegete. He acquired knowledge from his grandfather Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud, and he was attentive in recording his grandfather's gems and collecting his benefits. He commented on al-Wiqayah from the works of his grandfather Taj al-Shari'ah, then he abridged it and named it al-Niqayah. And he authored in usul a matn named al-Tanqih, then he composed a commentary named al-Tawdih. He died in the year 747 AH. The resting place of his parents, children, and ancestors is in Shahr Abad, Bukhara. As for his grandfather (his father's father) Taj al-Shari'ah and his maternal grandfather Burhan al-Din, they died in Kerman and were buried there—thus mentioned by Abd al-Baqi al-Khatib in al-Madinah al-Munawwarah. And in Madinat al-Ulum: Among the commentaries of al-Hidayah is Nihayat al-Kifayah by Taj al-Shari'ah, who is Mahmud. He was a scholar, virtuous, perfect. He also authored an abridgment of al-Hidayah called al-Wiqayah. I say: All this text indicates that the author of al-Wiqayah is the commentator of al-Hidayah, Taj al-Shari'ah, and his name is Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar, and that he is the grandfather of Sadr al-Shari'ah, the commentator of al-Wiqayah, on his father's side. The well-known (but incorrect) opinion is that the author of al-Wiqayah is the 'corrupt grandfather' of the commentator of al-Wiqayah. Al-Qahistani explicitly stated in Jami' al-Rumuz: 'The commentator of al-Wiqayah is Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah Umar ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah, and the author of al-Wiqayah is Burhan al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah, brother of Taj al-Shari'ah.' Similarly, the author of al-Kashf mentioned: 'Al-Wiqayah is by Imam Burhan al-Din Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah, compiled for the sake of his daughter's son Sadr al-Shari'ah.' Allah knows the truth of the matter. I have verified the matter through the declarations of reliable scholars in the introduction to my commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, so consult it.

Fa'idah: 'Sadr al-Shari'ah' is a title famous for two individuals: one is described as Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar and Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Awwal, and he is Ahmad ibn Jamal al-Din Ubayd Allah al-Mahbubi, who is the father of Taj al-Shari'ah. The second is described as Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar and Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Thani, and he is the commentator of al-Wiqayah, Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar. Thus in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a detailed biographical entry for the author known as Sahib al-Wiqayah. It begins by identifying him as Imam Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad, from a scholarly family. He wrote al-Wiqayah, a selection from al-Hidayah, for his grandson Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah, who later wrote a commentary on it. The entry then discusses the life and works of the grandson, who also authored important usul works like al-Tanqih and its commentary al-Tawdih. A significant part of this passage is dedicated to correcting a genealogical error: some scholars, like al-Qahistani, claimed that the author of al-Wiqayah was Burhan al-Din Mahmud (brother of Taj al-Shari'ah), but the author asserts based on reliable sources that the author is indeed Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud. The fa'idah clarifies that the title 'Sadr al-Shari'ah' refers to two persons: the elder (Ahmad, father of Taj al-Shari'ah) and the younger (Ubayd Allah, the commentator of al-Wiqayah). This lesson provides a careful genealogical and chronological clarification important for Hanafi biographical studies.

Key Terms
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Shari'ah): A title used for two Hanafi scholars: the elder (Ahmad) and the younger (Ubayd Allah), distinguished by 'al-Akbar' and 'al-Asghar'.
تاج الشريعة (Taj al-Shari'ah): Title of Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad, author of al-Wiqayah.
الوقاية (al-Wiqayah): A renowned Hanafi fiqh text, an abridgment of al-Hidayah by Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's verification, who is the correct author of al-Wiqayah?
A) Burhan al-Din Mahmud
B) Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud
C) Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah
D) Sadr al-Shari'ah Ahmad

Key Takeaway
Accurate attribution of classical texts like al-Wiqayah relies on careful verification of genealogical and biographical details.

Biographies of Key Hanafi Authorities: al-Marghinani and Sadr al-Din Sulayman
Biographical entries for two Hanafi authorities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scholarly contributions of Ali ibn Abi Bakr al-Marghinani and Sadr al-Din Sulayman ibn Wahb, and explain their significance for Hanafi ifta practice.

Core Idea
Two towering figures: al-Marghinani, the mujtahid author of al-Hidayah, and Sadr al-Din Sulayman, the chief judge who led Hanafi fiqh in Egypt and Syria.

This lesson introduces two pivotal figures in the Hanafi tradition: Ali ibn Abi Bakr al-Marghinani, known as Sahib al-Hidayah, and Sadr al-Din Sulayman ibn Wahb. Both played critical roles in shaping Hanafi jurisprudence and its transmission. Understanding their biographies helps us appreciate the authority behind the texts and rulings we study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scholars
Read the passage and note the names, epithets, and key biographical details for each.
2
Analyze al-Marghinani's scholarly rank
Examine the qualities attributed to him: imam, faqih, muhaddith, etc. Note the dispute about his being counted as a mujtahid or ashab al-tarjih.
This is a point of legitimate ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze Sadr al-Din Sulayman's role
Note his teachers, students, judicial positions, and writings. Understand his role as a leading Hanafi authority in his time.
4
Connect to ifta practice
Consider how the authority of these scholars affects the reliability of the texts and rulings they transmitted and authored.
Al-Hidayah is a primary reference for Hanafi muftis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب الهداية : هو على بن أبى بكر بن عبد الجليل الفرغاني المرغيناني . كان إماماً ، فقيها ، حافظا، محدثا ، مفسراً، جامعا للعلوم، ضابطا للفنون، متقنا ، نظاراً، أصوليا ، أديبا ، شاعراً ، لم تر العيون مثله في الأدب، وله اليد الباسطة في الخلاف والباع الممتد في المذهب . توفي سنة ٥٩٣هـ . عده ابن كمال باشا من أصحاب الترجيح. وتعقب بأن شأنه ليس أدنى من قاضيخان، وله في نقد الدلائل واستخراج المسائل شأن أى شأن! فهو أحق بالاجتهاد في المذهب، وعده من المجتهدين في المذهب إلى العقل السليم أقرب .

صدر الدین سلیمان : هو صدر الدین سلیمان بن وهب قال في الفوائد سليمان بن وهب قاضي القضاة صدر الدين أبو الربيع، تفقه على محمود ابن عبد السيد الحصيري تلميذ ،قاضیخان وصنف منتخب شرح الزيادات الذي ألفه ،قاضیخان، وتفقه عليه ابنه محمد بن سليمان، وأحمد بن إبراهيم السروجي، وتولى القضاء بمصر والشام وعاش ثلاثا وثمانين سنة، ومات سنة سبع وسبعين وستمائة . قال الجامع : هو سليمان الصدر بن أبي العز وهب بن عطاء الأزرعي، كذا ذكره السيوطي في "حسن المحاضرة " ، وقال : قال الصغدي : كان إماماً عالمًا متبحراً عارفا بدقائق الفقه وغوامضه انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية بمصر والشام. تفقه على الجمال الحصيري وغيره وسكن مصر وولّى قضاء العسكر بها وقضاء الشام. له مؤلفات
Sahib al-Hidayah: He is Ali ibn Abi Bakr ibn Abd al-Jalil al-Farghani al-Marghinani. He was an imam, jurist, memorizer, hadith scholar, exegete, comprehensive of sciences, master of arts, precise, reflective, usuli, literary, poet. Eyes have not seen the like of him in literature. He had an extensive hand in ikhtilaf and a long reach in the madhhab. He died in the year 593 AH. Ibn Kamal Basha counted him among the 'as hab al-tarjih (those capable of tarjih). It is objected that his status is not less than Qadikhan. He has great stature in criticizing evidences and deriving issues! So he is more deserving of ijtihad in the madhhab. Counting him among the mujtahids in the madhhab is closer to sound reason.

Sadr al-Din Sulayman: He is Sadr al-Din Sulayman ibn Wahb. He said in al-Fawa'id: Sulayman ibn Wahb, chief judge, Sadr al-Din Abu al-Rabi'. He studied fiqh under Mahmud ibn Abd al-Sayyid al-Husayri, student of Qadikhan. He authored a selection from the commentary on al-Ziyadat that Qadikhan had written. His son Muhammad ibn Sulayman and Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Saruji studied fiqh under him. He undertook the judiciary in Egypt and Syria and lived eighty-three years, dying in the year 677 AH. The compiler said: He is Sulayman al-Sadr ibn Abi al-Izz Wahb ibn Ata' al-Azra'i. Thus al-Suyuti mentioned in Husn al-Muhadarah, and he said: al-Saghdai said: He was an imam, learned, profound, knowledgeable of the subtleties of fiqh and its intricacies. The leadership of the Hanafis in Egypt and Syria culminated in him. He studied fiqh under al-Jamal al-Husayri and others, resided in Egypt, and held the position of judge of the army there and the judiciary of Syria. He has writings.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage contains two biographical entries. The first is for Sahib al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani, the renowned author of the foundational Hanafi work al-Hidayah. It highlights his mastery in many fields, especially his skill in handling ikhtilaf (disputed issues) and his deep knowledge of the madhhab. The text notes that Ibn Kamal Basha counted him among those capable of tarjih (preferring one opinion over another), and this is defended as appropriate given his stature. The second entry is for Sadr al-Din Sulayman ibn Wahb, a chief judge and leading Hanafi scholar in Egypt and Syria. He studied under al-Husayri, authored a selection from a commentary on al-Ziyadat, and had distinguished students. He served as judge and lived a long life. Both entries are straightforward biographical summaries.

Key Terms
صاحب الهداية (Sahib al-Hidayah): The author of the Hanafi fiqh work al-Hidayah, i.e., Ali ibn Abi Bakr al-Marghinani.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of preferring one legal opinion over another based on evidence.
اجتهاد في المذهب (ijtihad fi al-madhhab): Independent reasoning within the bounds of the Hanafi school, where the scholar derives rulings using the school's principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about Sadr al-Din Sulayman?
A) He was a student of al-Marghinani.
B) He wrote a commentary on al-Hidayah.
C) He served as judge in Egypt and Syria.
D) He died in 593 AH.

Key Takeaway
Al-Marghinani and Sadr al-Din Sulayman represent two pillars of Hanafi authority: textual scholarship and judicial practice.

Distinguishing the Two Sadr al-Shari'ah Scholars
Biographical clarification distinguishing two scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi scholars known as Sadr al-Shari'ah and distinguish between al-Akbar and al-Asghar using their full names and key works.

Core Idea
Two Hanafi scholars share the title Sadr al-Shari'ah: the elder (grandfather) and the younger (grandson, commentator on al-Wiqayah).

In Hanafi biographical literature, the title 'Sadr al-Shari'ah' is shared by two distinguished scholars. Without careful distinction, one might conflate them, leading to errors in attributing works and positions. This lesson clarifies their identities and lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two individuals
Read the passage and note that two scholars are described as Sadr al-Shari'ah. One is called al-Akbar (older) and the other al-Asghar (younger).
Remember that titles like 'al-Akbar' and 'al-Asghar' are relative.
2
Extract full names and family links
From the text, write down the full name of each: Ahmad ibn Jamal al-Din 'Ubayd Allah al-Mahbubi (al-Akbar) and 'Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar (al-Asghar). Note that the younger is the grandson of the elder.
Taj al-Shari'ah is the son of the elder and father of the younger.
3
Recognize key works
Identify that the younger Sadr al-Shari'ah (al-Asghar) is the commentator on al-Wiqayah (Sharh al-Wiqayah). The elder is the father of Taj al-Shari'ah.
This commentary is a major Hanafi text.
4
Apply the distinction
When encountering a reference to Sadr al-Shari'ah in a Hanafi source, use context (e.g., mention of Sharh al-Wiqayah) to determine which scholar is intended.
This prevents misattribution of opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محمود بن صدر الشريعة صنّفه لأجل ابن بنته صدر الشريعة". والله أعلم بحقيقة الحال، وقد حققت الأمر بتصريحات الثقاة في مقدمة شرحي لشرح الوقاية، فلتطالع . كذا في النافع الكبير لمن يطالع الجامع الصغير " + فائدة : صدر الشريعة اشتهر به اثنان يوصف أحدهما بصدر الشريعة الأكبر، وصدر الشريعة الأول، وهو أحمد بن جمال الدين عبيد الله المحبوبي، وهو والد تاج الشريعة" ، وثانيهما يوصف بصدر الشريعة الأصغر، وصدر الشريعة الثاني : وهو شارح الوقاية عبيد الله بن مسعود بن تاج الشريعة محمود بن صدر الشريعة الأكبر، كذا في "الفوائد البهية " .
Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah authored it for his grandson Sadr al-Shari'ah. And Allah knows the reality, and I have verified the matter with the statements of reliable sources in the introduction of my commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, so refer to it. Likewise in al-Nafi' al-Kabir for whoever reads al-Jami' al-Saghir. + Benefit: Sadr al-Shari'ah became famous for two [scholars], one described as Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar and the first, he is Ahmad ibn Jamal al-Din 'Ubayd Allah al-Mahbubi, and he is the father of Taj al-Shari'ah; and the second is described as Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Asghar and the second, he is the commentator on al-Wiqayah, 'Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud ibn Taj al-Shari'ah Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar, as in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage clarifies the identity of two Hanafi scholars both known as Sadr al-Shari'ah. The first is the grandfather (al-Akbar, Ahmad ibn Jamal al-Din) and the second is the grandson (al-Asghar, 'Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud) who wrote the famous commentary on al-Wiqayah. The text also mentions a book authored by Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah for his grandson.

Key Terms
صدر الشريعة (Sadr al-Shari'ah): Title meaning 'Chest of the Shari'ah', applied to two Hanafi scholars distinguished as al-Akbar (elder) and al-Asghar (younger).
تاج الشريعة (Taj al-Shari'ah): Title meaning 'Crown of the Shari'ah', used for Mahmud ibn Sadr al-Shari'ah al-Akbar, the father of the younger Sadr al-Shari'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 'Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud

Key Takeaway
Two Hanafi scholars share the title Sadr al-Shari'ah: the elder Ahmad and the younger 'Ubayd Allah, who commented on al-Wiqayah.

The Author of al-Hidayah: Ali al-Marghinani
Biographical entry on the author of al-Hidayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Ali al-Marghinani and state the two positions regarding his rank in the Hanafi madhhab (ashab al-tarjih vs. mujtahid fil-madhhab).

Core Idea
Al-Marghinani's rank is debated: was he a mujtahid in the madhhab or an expert of tarjih?

The author of al-Hidayah, Ali al-Marghinani, is a towering figure in the Hanafi school. His text is so central that knowing his scholarly rank helps us understand the weight of his opinions. This passage sketches his extraordinary qualifications and records a key debate: was he merely an arbiter between conflicting rulings, or did he have the authority of a mujtahid within the madhhab?

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his works
Read the full name: Ali ibn Abi Bakr ibn Abd al-Jalil al-Farghani al-Marghinani. Note his most famous work: al-Hidayah.
Al-Hidayah is a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and one of the most relied-upon texts in the Hanafi madhhab.
2
List his scholarly qualifications
The text lists multiple titles: imam, faqih, hafiz, muhaddith, mufassir, usuli, adib, poet. This shows comprehensive mastery.
Such versatility is rare; it indicates his ability to derive rulings from primary sources.
3
Identify the two positions on his rank
Ibn Kamal Pasha counted him among ashab al-tarjih (experts who weigh between opinions). An objection argues he was at least as qualified as Qadikhan and should be considered a mujtahid fil-madhhab.
The objector emphasizes his skill in naqd al-dalail (critiquing evidences) and istikhraj al-masail (extracting rulings).
4
Evaluate which position is stronger according to the text
The passage leans toward the higher rank: 'He is more deserving of ijtihad in the madhhab.' This suggests al-Marghinani had ijtihad authority within the school.
This affects how we treat his rulings – they are not mere preferences but carry greater weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
-٥٦ صاحب الهداية : هو على بن أبى بكر بن عبد الجليل الفرغاني المرغيناني . كان إماماً ، فقيها ، حافظا، محدثا ، مفسراً، جامعا للعلوم، ضابطا للفنون، متقنا ، نظاراً، أصوليا ، أديبا ، شاعراً ، لم تر العيون مثله في الأدب، وله اليد الباسطة في الخلاف والباع الممتد في المذهب . توفي سنة ٥٩٣هـ . عده ابن كمال باشا من أصحاب الترجيح. وتعقب بأن شأنه ليس أدنى من قاضيخان، وله في نقد الدلائل واستخراج المسائل شأن أى شأن! فهو أحق بالاجتهاد في المذهب، وعده من المجتهدين في المذهب إلى العقل السليم أقرب .
56. The author of al-Hidayah: He is Ali ibn Abi Bakr ibn Abd al-Jalil al-Farghani al-Marghinani. He was an imam, a jurist, a memorizer, a hadith scholar, a mufassir, a comprehensive scholar, a master of various arts, precise, a contemplator, a usuli, a literary man, a poet; eyes have not seen the like of him in literature. He had a vast hand in ikhtilaf and an extended reach in the madhhab. He died in 593 AH. Ibn Kamal Pasha counted him among the specialists of tarjih. It was objected that his stature is not lower than Qadikhan, and he has a significant role in critiquing evidences and extracting issues! So he is more deserving of ijtihad in the madhhab, and counting him among the mujtahids in the madhhab is closer to sound reason.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage provides a high praise of Ali al-Marghinani, the author of al-Hidayah, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. It highlights his mastery in various fields and notes the debate about his rank: Ibn Kamal Pasha considered him a specialist in tarjih (preference), but some argue he was actually a mujtahid within the madhhab, comparable to Qadikhan.

Key Terms
الهداية (al-Hidayah): The famous Hanafi fiqh text by al-Marghinani, a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
أصحاب الترجيح (ashab al-tarjih): Scholars who weigh and prefer between different opinions within the madhhab.
المجتهد في المذهب (al-mujtahid fil-madhhab): A scholar qualified to derive rulings within the framework of the madhhab's principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 603 AH
C) 583 AH
D) 613 AH

Key Takeaway
Al-Marghinani's status as a mujtahid in the madhhab is strongly supported, making al-Hidayah a primary source for fatwa.

Biography of Sadr al-Din Sulayman ibn Wahb
Biographical entry on a Hanafi jurist

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scholarly lineage and contributions of Sadr al-Din Sulayman ibn Wahb to the Hanafi school and explain his significance in the iftaa tradition.

Core Idea
A key link in the Hanafi chain who authored a critical abridgement of Qadikhan's Sharh al-Ziyadat.

This lesson introduces Sadr al-Din Sulayman ibn Wahb, a towering figure in Hanafi judiciary and scholarship. You will learn about his teachers, students, works, and the high judicial offices he held. Understanding his role helps you trace the transmission of Hanafi fiqh and the authority of later fatwa compilations.

Guided Path
1
Identify basic biographical data
Extract the full name, death date, and key teachers from the passage. Note that he died in 677 AH and studied under Mahmud ibn Abd al-Sayyid al-Khasiri.
Also note his son Muhammad ibn Sulayman and Ahmad al-Saruji as his students.
2
Identify his scholarly works
The passage mentions he authored an abridgement (muntakhab) of Qadikhan's Sharh al-Ziyadat. This is a significant work in the Hanafi corpus.
3
Trace his judicial career
He held the posts of qadi al-qudat in Egypt and Syria, indicating high authority in both judiciary and iftaa.
Chief judges often exerted great influence on fatwa practice.
4
Situate him in the Hanafi chain
He was a student of al-Khasiri (student of Qadikhan) and taught prominent Hanafis. This places him as a key transmitter of the madhhab's authoritative positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
-٥٧ صدر الدین سلیمان : هو صدر الدین سلیمان بن وهب قال في الفوائد سليمان بن وهب قاضي القضاة صدر الدين أبو الربيع، تفقه على محمود ابن عبد السيد الحصيري تلميذ ،قاضیخان وصنف منتخب شرح الزيادات الذي ألفه ،قاضیخان، وتفقه عليه ابنه محمد بن سليمان، وأحمد بن إبراهيم السروجي، وتولى القضاء بمصر والشام وعاش ثلاثا وثمانين سنة، ومات سنة سبع وسبعين وستمائة . قال الجامع : هو سليمان الصدر بن أبي العز وهب بن عطاء الأزرعي، كذا ذكره السيوطي في "حسن المحاضرة " ، وقال : قال الصغدي : كان إماماً عالمًا متبحراً عارفا بدقائق الفقه وغوامضه انتهت إليه رئاسة الحنفية بمصر والشام. تفقه على الجمال الحصيري وغيره وسكن مصر وولّى قضاء العسكر بها وقضاء الشام. له مؤلفات". وفي "مرآة الجنان" عند ذكر من توفى سنة ٦٧٧هـ: "شيخ الحنفية، قاضي القضاة، أبو الفضل سليمان بن أبي العز الأزرعى أحد من انتهت إليه رياسة المذهب في زمانه " . والله أعلم .
57. Sadr al-Din Sulayman: He is Sadr al-Din Sulayman ibn Wahb. It is said in al-Fawa'id: Sulayman ibn Wahb, the chief judge, Sadr al-Din Abu al-Rabi', studied fiqh under Mahmud ibn Abd al-Sayyid al-Khasiri, a student of Qadikhan, and authored the abridgement of Sharh al-Ziyadat which Qadikhan wrote. His son Muhammad ibn Sulayman and Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Saruji studied under him. He held judgeship in Egypt and Syria, lived eighty-three years, and died in 677 AH. The compiler said: He is Sulayman al-Sadr ibn Abi al-Izz Wahb ibn Ata' al-Azra'i, as al-Suyuti mentioned in Husn al-Muhadarah. He said: al-Saghdi said: He was an imam, a profound scholar, knowledgeable in the subtleties and intricacies of fiqh; the leadership of the Hanafis in Egypt and Syria ended with him. He studied under al-Jamal al-Khasiri and others, resided in Egypt, and served as qadi of the army there and qadi of Syria. He has authored works. And in Mir'at al-Jinan, when mentioning those who died in 677 AH: 'The shaykh of the Hanafis, the chief judge, Abu al-Fadl Sulayman ibn Abi al-Izz al-Azra'i, one to whom the leadership of the madhhab reached in his time.' And Allah knows best.

Commentary
This passage gives a detailed biography of Sadr al-Din Sulayman ibn Wahb, a prominent Hanafi jurist and judge. It notes his studies under al-Khasiri, his authorship of an abridgement of Qadikhan's Sharh al-Ziyadat, his teaching, and his high positions as qadi in Egypt and Syria. The text quotes multiple sources confirming his leadership in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
قاضي القضاة (qadi al-qudat): Chief judge, the highest judicial office.
شرح الزيادات (Sharh al-Ziyadat): A commentary by Qadikhan on Muhammad al-Shaybani's al-Ziyadat.
منتخب (muntakhab): An abridgement or selection; a condensed version of a larger work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Identifying al-Tahawi the Glossist
Biographical note on the Hanafi jurist al-Tahawi known for glosses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi commentator al-Tahawi and state his significance as a glossist on key Hanafi texts.

Core Idea
Al-Tahawi (d. 13th c. AH) authored glosses on al-Durr al-Mukhtar; not the early scholar of al-Aqidah.

This passage introduces a later Hanafi scholar, al-Tahawi, who lived in the 13th century AH. It highlights his role as a glossator (hashiyah) on two major works: al-Maraqi and al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The text also mentions his student and provides three conflicting reports of his death year, a common feature in biographical entries. Understanding who this al-Tahawi is helps avoid confusion with the more famous early Hanafi scholar of the same name.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar
Read the first line: who is al-Tahawi? The text says he is among the virtuous of the 13th century. Note the time period and his scholarly stature.
2
Recognize His Works
The passage states he wrote a gloss (hashiyah) on al-Maraqi and al-Durr al-Mukhtar. These are later Hanafi texts, showing his contribution to the madhhab's commentary tradition.
Al-Maraqi is a text on usul al-fiqh; al-Durr al-Mukhtar is a famous fiqh manual of the later Hanafi school.
3
Note the Scholarly Network
His student Abd al-Mawla al-Dimyati is mentioned as author of Ta'aliq al-Anwar. This indicates a chain of transmission and scholarly lineage.
4
Analyze the Death Date Discrepancy
The text cites three sources with different death years: 1243 AH, 1233 AH, and 1250 AH. This shows the uncertainty in biographical records and the importance of cross-referencing.
Mufid al-Mufti, al-Hada'iq, and Ghayth al-Ghamam are biographical sources. The variation may stem from different manuscript traditions or hearsay.
5
Distinguish from Other Scholars
This al-Tahawi is not the early Hanafi scholar Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH), author of al-Aqidah al-Tahawiyyah. The difference in era and works is critical.
The common misunderstanding is noted in the passage; always verify which Tahawi is being referenced.

الطحطاوي : هو من فضلاء القرن الثالث عشر، كما يظهر عن مطالعة كتاب الإجازات من رد المحتار، وله حاشية على المراقي" و "الدر المختار"، وقد تلمذ عليه عبد المولى بن عبد الله الدمياطي، صاحب تعاليق الأنوار على الدر المختار " . قال في مفيد المفتى : "إنه مات سنة ١٢٤٣هـ ، وقيل : سنة ١٢٣٣هـ، كما في "الحدائق". وفي غيث الغمام : أنه مات سنة ١٢٥٠هـ .

Under him studied Abd al-Mawla ibn Abd Allah al-Dimyati, the author of Ta'aliq al-Anwar on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. It is said in Mufid al-Mufti: 'He died in 1243 AH, and it is said: 1233 AH, as in al-Hada'iq. And in Ghayth al-Ghamam: he died in 1250 AH.'

Commentary
This short passage identifies al-Tahawi as a 13th-century Hanafi scholar known for his glosses on key Hanafi texts like al-Maraqi and al-Durr al-Mukhtar. It mentions his student and provides conflicting reports of his death year (1243, 1233, or 1250 AH), reflecting uncertainty in biographical sources.

Key Terms
حاشية (hashiyah): A gloss or supercommentary on a primary text.
الدر المختار (al-Durr al-Mukhtar): A famous Hanafi fiqh text by Haskafi, often commented upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Biography of al-Tarsusi and the Weight of His Fatwa Collection
Biographical entry with critical evaluation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the biography of Burhan al-Din al-Tarsusi and explain why Ibn al-Humam's criticism affects the authority of his fatwa collection in Hanafi practice.

Core Idea
A fatwa collection's authority may be questioned by later masters—knowing the scholar's background is essential for mufti's taqlid.

This lesson introduces Burhan al-Din al-Tarsusi, a Hanafi judge and author of a well-known fatwa collection. However, even a qadi's work can be subject to harsh critique from later jurists like Ibn al-Humam. Understanding such evaluations helps a mufti properly weigh sources when issuing fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Extract the biographical data
Identify the scholar's full name (Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Tarsusi), his title (qadi), his appointment as judge of Damascus in 746 AH, his scholarly activities (ifta, teaching), and his death year (758 AH).
2
Identify his authored work
Note the title of his fatwa collection: 'Anfa' al-Masa'il ila Tahrir al-Masa'il' (known as al-Fatawa al-Tarsusiyya). Understand that it is an abridgment arranged by fiqh chapters.
This work is a useful compilation but not a primary source of fiqh.
3
Analyze the critical remark
Read the quote from Ibn al-Humam via al-Shami: 'he was not among the people of fiqh.' Reflect on why such a statement from a leading Hanafi jurist undermines the reliability of al-Tarsusi's fatwas.
Ibn al-Humam's opinion carries weight in Hanafi scholarship; his critique suggests caution.
4
Examine the philological digression
Observe how the author meticulously verifies the pronunciation of 'Tarsus' by quoting multiple authorities. Understand that this precision reflects a scholarly concern for accuracy, even for place names.
This detail shows the compiler's care in transmission, but does not affect legal authority.
5
Synthesize the lesson for the mufti
Conclude that al-Fatawa al-Tarsusiyya, while useful, must be used with awareness of Ibn al-Humam's criticism. A mufti should prioritize stronger sources (e.g., works by Ibn al-Humam, al-Marghinani) when available.
This is a practical lesson in source hierarchy (zahir al-riwayah vs. later compilations).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
-٥٩- الطرطوسي : هو القاضى برهان الدين إبراهيم بن على الطرسوسي. ولى القضاء بـ"دمشق" بعد والده سنة ٧٤٦هـ وأفتى ودرس وصنف "أنفع المسائل إلى تحرير المسائل"، المعروف بالفتاوى الطرسوسية، وهو مختصر نافع، جمع فيه المسائل المهمة ورتبها على ترتيب الكتب الفقهية. مات سنة ٧٥٨هـ . كذا ذكره قاسم ابن قطلوبغا في ،ترجمته، وذكره عبد القادر" في "الجواهر المضيئة فى اب "أحمد ابن على " . والأول أصح. قال "الشامي": "أما الطرسوسي فقد صدق فيه قول المحقق ابن الهمام: إنه لم يكن من أهل الفقه فان هم . ونسبته إلى طرسوس (بفتح الطاء والراء المهملتين بعدها سين مهملة مضمومة بعدها واو بعدها سين مهملة كذا ضبطه النووى في تهذيب الأسماء واللغات" ، وابن خلكان في وفيات الأعيان"، وكذا ضبطه السمعاني وقال: "هى من بلاد "الثغر" بالشام، وكان يضرب بعيدها المثل ؛ لأنها "ثغر" وأهلها يتزينون ويخرجون بالأسلحة الكثيرة المليحة، والخيل الحسان؛ ليصل الخوف إلى الكفار" . وقال أبو محمد عبد الله بن مسلم، المعروف بابن قتيبة في أدب الكاتب : " وهى طرسوس، سلعوس سفوان وبرهوت باليمن كل ذلك بفتح ثانية
59. Al-Tartusi: He is the judge Burhan al-Din Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Tarsusi. He became judge of Damascus after his father in 746 AH, gave fatwas, taught, and authored 'Anfa' al-Masa'il ila Tahrir al-Masa'il', known as al-Fatawa al-Tarsusiyya, a useful abridgment in which he collected important issues and arranged them according to the order of fiqh books. The passage also includes a detailed philological discussion of the proper pronunciation and spelling of 'Tarsus' and other place names, quoting several authorities.

Key Terms

ابن الهمام (Ibn al-Humam): A prominent Hanafi jurist (d. 861 AH) known for his critical assessments.
برهان الدين إبراهيم بن علي الطرسوسي (Burhan al-Din Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Tarsusi): The full name of al-Tarsusi, a Hanafi judge and jurist.

Biography of al-Awza'i: A Memorization Anchor
Biographical entry of a prominent Syrian scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of al-Awza'i and explain his significance as an independent mujtahid whose views are cited in Hanafi ikhtilaf literature.

Core Idea
Al-Awza'i was the Imam of Syria and a founder of a madhhab, not a Hanafi; his knowledge is recorded for comparative fiqh.

This biography introduces Abd al-Rahman ibn Amr al-Awza'i, a towering figure of early Islamic scholarship. Although he established his own school of jurisprudence, his rulings and methods are frequently discussed in Hanafi works like Rasm al-Mufti. Understanding his life helps us appreciate the diversity of early ijtihad and the respect Hanafi scholars had for other mujtahidun.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full name and primary titles
Note his kunya (Abu Amr) and his nisba (al-Awza'i). This is the basic identification needed when encountering his name in fiqh texts.
2
Locate his geographical and educational background
He was born in Baalbek (88 or 93 AH), raised in the Biqa valley, then moved to Beirut. He became the leading scholar of Syria.
His Syrian context is important because regional differences often influenced fiqh.
3
Assess his scholarly output
He reportedly answered 70,000 legal questions, indicating encyclopedic knowledge. This explains why his views are cited in ikhtilaf literature.
The number symbolises his authority, not a precise count.
4
Understand the story of his death
The incident in the bathhouse has legal implications regarding handling the deceased: his wife moved his body to face the qibla unintentionally, and Sa'id ibn Abd al-Aziz ordered her to free a slave.
This story is often referenced in fiqh of janaza.
5
Clarify the origin of his nisba
He was not from the Awza' tribe or village but resided among them, hence the attribution. This is a common pattern in nisba formation.
Memorize the spelling: فتح الهمزة وسكون الواو وفتح الزاء.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عبد الرحمن بن عمرو الأوزاعي : هو أبو عمرو إمام أهل الشام لم يكن بالشام أعلم منه . قيل : إنه أجاب في سبعين ألف مسألة . وكان يسكن بيروت، وكانت ولادته ببعلبك سنة ٨٨هـ . وقيل : سنة ٩٣هـ . ومنشأه بالبقاع ثم نقلته أمه إلى بيروت، وكان فوق الربعة، خفيف اللحية، به سمرة، وكان يخضب بالحناء. وتوفى سنة ١٥٧هـ ، يوم الأحد لليلتين بقيتا من صفر . وقيل : في شهر ربيع الأول بمدينة بيروت، وقبره في قرية على باب بيروت يقال لها : "حنتوس"، وأهلها مسلمون، وهو مدفون في قبلة المسجد، وأهل القرية لا يعرفونه، بل يقولون : ههنا رجل صالح ينزل عليه النور، ولا يعرفه إلا الخواص من الناس. ذكر الحافظ ابن عساکر في تاريخ دمشق : أن الأوزاعي دخل الحمام ببيروت، وكان لصاحب الحمام شغل فأغلق الحمام عليه وذهب، ثم جاء ففتح الباب فوجده ميتا قد وضع يده اليمنى تحت خده، وهو مستقبل القبلة ، وقيل : إن امرأته فعلت ذلك ولم تكن عامدة لذلك، فأمرها سعيد بن عبد العزيز لعتق رقبة. والأوزاعي (بفتح الهمزة وسكون الواو وفتح الزاء وبعد الألف عين مهملة) هذه النسبة إلى "أوزاع وهى بطن ذى الكلاع من اليمن . وقيل : بطن من " همدان" واسمه مرثد بن زيد وقيل : الأوزاع قرية بدمشق على طريق باب "الفراديس " ولم يكن أبو عمرو منهم، وإنما ينزل فيهم فنسب إليهم . وهو سبى من اليمن، كذا في رفيات الأعيان لابن خلكان، ومثله فى حياة الحيوان للدميري فليحفظ .
Abd al-Rahman ibn Amr al-Awza'i: He is Abu Amr, the Imam of the people of Syria; there was no one in Syria more knowledgeable than him. It is said that he answered seventy thousand legal questions. He lived in Beirut, and his birth was in Baalbek in 88 AH. Some say 93 AH. His origin was in the Biqa valley, then his mother moved him to Beirut. He was above average height, with a light beard, of brown complexion, and he used to dye with henna. He died in 157 AH, on Sunday with two nights remaining in Safar. Some say in the month of Rabi al-Awwal in the city of Beirut. His grave is in a village at the gate of Beirut called 'Hantous'; its inhabitants are Muslims, and he is buried in the qibla direction of the mosque. The villagers do not know him, rather they say: 'Here is a righteous man upon whom light descends,' and only the elite know him. Al-Hafiz Ibn Asakir mentioned in Tarikh Dimashq that al-Awza'i entered a bathhouse in Beirut, and the bathhouse owner was busy, so he locked the bathhouse on him and left. Then he came and opened the door and found him dead, having placed his right hand under his cheek, facing the qibla. It is also said that his wife did that unintentionally, so Sa'id ibn Abd al-Aziz ordered her to free a slave. Al-Awza'i (with fatha on the hamza, sukun on the waw, fatha on the zay, and after the alif an important 'ayn) this nisba is to 'Awza', which is a sub-tribe of Dhu al-Kila' from Yemen. Or a sub-tribe of Hamdan, and his name is Murthid ibn Zayd. It is also said that Awza' is a village in Damascus on the road to Bab al-Faradis. Abu Amr was not from them, but he resided among them, so he was attributed to them. He was a captive from Yemen. This is in Wafayat al-A'yan by Ibn Khallikan, and similar in Hayat al-Hayawan by al-Damiri, so let it be memorized.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about Abd al-Rahman ibn Amr al-Awza'i (d. 157 AH), a prominent Syrian scholar and founder of the Awza'i school of jurisprudence, which was dominant in Syria before being superseded by the Shafi'i school. The author includes him because his name appears in the commentary on Rasm al-Mufti, likely in discussions of ikhtilaf. The biography notes his immense knowledge (reportedly answering 70,000 questions), his physical description, and the details of his death in a bathhouse. The story of his wife moving his body to face the qibla is significant in fiqh for rulings on handling the deceased. The explanation of the nisba 'al-Awza'i' is also typical of biographical dictionaries. While not a Hanafi himself, al-Awza'i is frequently cited in Hanafi works for comparative fiqh.

Key Terms
الأوزاعي (al-Awza'i): The nisba of Abd al-Rahman ibn Amr, the Syrian Imam, attributed to the tribe or village of Awza'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 70,000
C) 700,000
D) 17,000

Key Takeaway
Al-Awza'i was a major independent scholar whose biography is memorized to recognize his role in early ijtihad and his citation in Hanafi ikhtilaf works.

Biography of Ibn al-Mubarak
Biographical entry of a major Hanafi hadith scholar and ascetic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical facts of Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak and explain his significance for the Hanafi tradition of knowledge transmission.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Mubarak's journey from musician to ascetic scholar exemplifies the Quranic call for heart's humility — a foundational trait for a mufti.

This lesson introduces you to Abdallah ibn al-Mubarak, a towering figure in hadith, fiqh, and zuhd. His biography is not merely historical; it illustrates the personal transformation required for one who carries sacred knowledge. In the Hanafi usul al-ifta tradition, knowing the characters of our predecessors reinforces the chain of transmission and the ethics of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify his full name and lineage
Locate his kunya (Abu Abd al-Rahman), nasab (al-Marwazi), tribal affiliation (mawla of a man from Hanzala), mother's origin (Khwarazm), father's origin (Turkish).
2
Note birth and death dates
Born 118 AH, died 181 AH. These dates anchor him in the early Abbasid period.
3
Recognize teacher-student connections
He accompanied Abu Hanifa and took knowledge from him; he was also a teacher of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal.
This places him in the Hanafi chain of transmission.
4
Recall the repentance story
He describes a dream where a bird recites Quran 57:16, prompting him to break his musical instruments and begin asceticism.
The partial verse is in the passage.
5
Understand his status
Al-Dhahabi calls him one of the pillars of the Ummah in knowledge, hadith, and asceticism.
This justifies his inclusion in a usul al-ifta work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عبد الله بن المبارك : هو أبو عبد الرحمن المروزى ولد سنة ثمان عشرة ومائة . هو مولى لرجل من حنظلة، وأمه خوارزمية. وأبوه كان تركيا . صاحب أبا حنيفة وأخذ عنه علمه، نظر إليه أبو حنيفة وسأله عن بدء أموره . فقال : كنت جالسا مع إخواني في البستان فأكلنا وشربنا إلى الليل، وكنت مولعا بضرب العود والطنبور . ونمت سحراً فرأيت في منامي طائراً فوق رأسى على شجرة يقول : ألم يَأْنِ لِلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا أَن تَخشَعَ قُلُوبُهُم لذكر الله وما نَزَلَ مِنَ الحق قلت: بلى، فانتبهت وكسرت عودى وأحرقت ما كان عندي فكان هذا أول زهدى قال الذهبي في حقه : إنه أحد أركان هذه الأمة في العلم والحديث والزهد، وأحد شيوخ الإمام أحمد أخذ عن أبي حنيفة، ومدحه في مواضع. وشهد له الأئمة. مات سنة ١٨١هـ. وقبره بـ "هيت" وهى مدينة مشهورة على الفرات .
Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak: He is Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Marwazi, born in the year 118 AH. He was a mawla of a man from Hanzala, and his mother was from Khwarazm. His father was Turkish. He accompanied Abu Hanifa and took knowledge from him. Abu Hanifa looked at him and asked him about the beginning of his affair. He said: I was sitting with my brothers in a garden, and we ate and drank until night, and I was fond of playing the oud and tanbur. Then I slept at dawn and saw in my dream a bird above my head on a tree saying: 'Has not the time come for those who believe that their hearts should be humbled at the remembrance of Allah and what has come down of the truth?' I said: Yes. So I awoke and broke my oud and burned what I had with me, and that was the beginning of my asceticism. Al-Dhahabi said about him: He is one of the pillars of this Ummah in knowledge, hadith, and asceticism, and one of the teachers of Imam Ahmad. He took from Abu Hanifa and praised him in several places. The Imams testified to him. He died in 181 AH. His grave is in 'Hit', a well-known city on the Euphrates.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage presents the biography of Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak (d. 181 AH), a towering figure in hadith, fiqh, and zuhd (asceticism). He was a student of Imam Abu Hanifa, and his inclusion in a Hanafi usul al-ifta work underscores the chain of knowledge. The narrative of his repentance from music and frivolity to asceticism is famous; it illustrates the concept of tawba and the transformation of a scholar. Al-Dhahabi's praise highlights his stature. His grave in Hit is a known landmark. For the Hanafi tradition, Ibn al-Mubarak is an important transmitter of Abu Hanifa's teachings, though he is also an independent hadith master.

Key Terms
ابن المبارك (Ibn al-Mubarak): Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, a famous hadith scholar, ascetic, and student of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He heard a lecture by Abu Hanifa
B) He saw a bird reciting a Quranic verse in a dream
C) He lost all his wealth
D) He was criticized by his teacher

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Mubarak's biography reminds us that true knowledge is accompanied by personal transformation (tawba) and connection to the scholarly chain.

Biography of 'Isam ibn Yusuf: A Window into Early Hanafi Diversity
Biographical entry for a Hanafi scholar, with notes on raf' al-yadayn ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of 'Isam ibn Yusuf and explain how his practice of raising hands in prayer illustrates internal diversity within the early Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Even early Hanafi masters differed on subsidiary issues like raising hands in prayer.

This lesson introduces you to 'Isam ibn Yusuf, a second-generation Hanafi scholar from Balkh. His biography is not just a list of dates and names; it reveals the living fabric of early Hanafi scholarship, where ikhtilaf existed even among direct students of Abu Hanifa. The detail about his practice of raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) is a concrete example that challenges the stereotype of a monolithic early school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his lineage
Locate the name 'Isam ibn Yusuf and note his kunya (Abu 'Isma) and his relationship to Ibrahim ibn Yusuf. This step establishes his identity within the Hanafi network.
He is the brother of Ibrahim, another Hanafi scholar in Balkh.
2
Trace his teachers and students
Identify who he narrated from (Ibn al-Mubarak, al-Thawri, Shu'ba) and who narrated from him (people of Balkh). This shows his role in transmitting hadith and fiqh.
His teachers are major hadith masters, indicating his credibility in hadith.
3
Note the ikhtilaf on raf' al-yadayn
The text explicitly states that 'Isam raised his hands at ruku' and after, while his brother Ibrahim did not. This is a direct example of ikhtilaf among Hanafis.
The mainstream Hanafi position is not to raise hands except for the opening takbir, but early figures differed.
4
Resolve the death date discrepancy
Two dates are given: 210 AH (al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya) and 215 AH (al-'Ayni). Note that such differences are common in early biographical sources and require tarjih based on reliability.
Ibn 'Abidin's Radd al-Muhtar confirms his association with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, which supports an earlier date.
5
Assess the relevance for iftaa
Understanding that 'Isam held a minority view helps a mufti contextualize that the Hanafi school historically accommodated some diversity. This knowledge prevents oversimplification when citing Hanafi positions.
In fatwa, the mufta bihi is the majority view, but awareness of minority views enriches scholarly depth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عصام بن يوسف : هو أبو عصمة البلخي، أخو إبراهيم بن يوسف، كانا شیخی بلخ في زمانهما بغیر مدافع لهما، وكان عصام يروى عن ابن المبارك والثورى وشعبة، وروى عنه أهل بلده وكان صاحب حديث، ثبتا في الرواية، وربما أخطأ وكان يرفع يديه عند الركوع وعند رفع الرأس منه، وأخوه إبراهيم كان لا يرفع . ومات عصام سنة ٢١٠هـ ، كذا في الفوائد البهية. وقال العيني في البناية : ومات عصام ببلخ سنة ٢١٥هـ، وكان أستاذ النصير ومحمد بن سلمة . وقال ابن عابدين في المجلد الثالث من رد المحتار: هو عصام بن يوسف من أصحاب أبي يوسف ومحمد، ومن أقران محمد ابن سماعة وابن رستم وأبي حفص البخارى".
'Isam ibn Yusuf: He is Abu 'Isma al-Balkhi, brother of Ibrahim ibn Yusuf. They were the two shaykhs of Balkh in their time, without dispute. 'Isam narrated from Ibn al-Mubarak, al-Thawri, and Shu'ba, and the people of his town narrated from him. He was a master of hadith, reliable in narration, though he sometimes made mistakes. He used to raise his hands at the time of bowing (ruku') and when raising his head from it, whereas his brother Ibrahim did not raise them. 'Isam died in 210 AH, according to al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya. Al-'Ayni said in al-Binaya: 'Isam died in Balkh in 215 AH, and he was the teacher of al-Nasir and Muhammad ibn Salama. Ibn 'Abidin said in the third volume of Radd al-Muhtar: He is 'Isam ibn Yusuf, one of the companions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and a contemporary of Muhammad ibn Sama'a, Ibn Rustam, and Abu Hafs al-Bukhari.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This is a biographical entry for 'Isam ibn Yusuf (d. 210/215 AH), a Hanafi scholar from Balkh. He is noted for being a hadith scholar and a student of major figures like Ibn al-Mubarak. The detail about raising hands in prayer (raf' al-yadayn) is interesting: he practiced it, while his brother did not. This reflects the known ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school: the preferred position is not to raise the hands except for the opening takbir, but some Hanafis like 'Isam followed the Shafi'i practice. The disagreement on his death date (210 or 215) is typical of early biographical sources. Ibn 'Abidin confirms he was a direct student of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, placing him in the second generation of Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms
عصام بن يوسف ('Isam ibn Yusuf): A Hanafi scholar from Balkh, student of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during prayer, specifically at the time of bowing (ruku') and after.
الفوائد البهية (Al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya): A biographical dictionary of Hanafi scholars compiled by al-Laknawi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 'Isam raised his hands at ruku' and after, Ibrahim did not.
C) 'Isam prayed with hands folded, Ibrahim did not.
D) 'Isam recited aloud, Ibrahim silently.

Key Takeaway
The biography of 'Isam ibn Yusuf shows that even among the earliest Hanafi authorities, there was diversity on subsidiary matters like raising hands in prayer, reminding us that the school's positions developed through later tarjih.

The Layers of Hanafi Scholars: Mujtahids and Muqallids
Biographical entry with tabaqa classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the layers of Hanafi scholars (mujtahid vs muqallid capable of tarjih) using the criteria from this biographical glossary.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, not all scholars have the same rank—some are absolute mujtahids, others are muqallids who perform tarjih.

This lesson uses the biographical entry of 'Ali al-Razi from the glossary to clarify the hierarchy of Hanafi scholars. The author of al-Hidayah classified scholars into layers, separating those who can perform ijtihad from those who exercise tarjih within the school. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for a mufti to know which opinions carry more weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's classification of 'Ali al-Razi
Read the entry on 'Ali al-Razi. The text explicitly states that he is among the first layers of muqallids (طبقات المقلدين) who are people of tarjih, not mujtahids.
The author of al-Hidayah is cited as the source of this classification.
2
List the scholars considered mujtahids
From the same entry, note the list of scholars who are considered mujtahids in the school: al-Khassaf, al-Tahawi, al-Karkhi, al-Sarakhsi, al-Halwani, Qadikhan, and others.
These are the absolute mujtahids in the madhhab.
3
List the scholars considered muqallids with tarjih
The entry mentions Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah as examples of muqallids who perform tarjih. The commentator adds that later scholars like Mulla Kamal are also included.
These scholars do not create new rules but prefer among existing ones.
4
Understand the principle: merit over chronology
The text explicitly states that ranks are by virtue and perfection (بالفضل والكمال), not by ancient times. This means even later scholars can be elevated if they possess the necessary qualification.
This is a key point for modern Hanafi fiqh.

الأعلام الوارد ذكرهم في الشرح

قُلُوبُهُم لذكر الله وما نَزَلَ مِنَ الحق قلت: بلى، فانتبهت وكسرت عودى وأحرقت ما عندي فكان هذا أول زهدى

توفى ليلة الاثنين سنة ٥٩٢هـ . عده كمال باشا من طبقة المجتهدين في المسائل. وقال قاسم ابن قطلوبغا في تصحيح القدورى " : "ما يصححه قاضيخان مقدم على تصحيح غيره ؛ لأنه فقيه النفس".

He wrote Kitab al-Salat. Al-Bazdawi is 'Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn 'Abd al-Karim ibn Musa. He was born around 400 AH, died on the 5th of Rajab 482 AH, and his coffin was carried to Samarkand. See also Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Fakhr al-Islam in the book index. 66 Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan: He is al-Hasan ibn Mansur ibn Mahmud al-Uzjandi al-Farghani, famous as Qadikhan. He was born in 802 AH in Cairo. His father died while he was young, so he memorized the Quran and books and presented them to
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a biographical glossary (الأعلام) of notable Hanafi scholars mentioned in the commentary (Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti). It is typical in classical Hanafi works to include such a section to establish the authority and chain of transmission of the scholars whose views are cited. The entries provide death dates, teachers, students, and sometimes opinions about the scholar's rank. For instance, 'Isam ibn Yusuf is noted for his practice of raising hands in prayer, contrasting with his brother, illustrating differences even among early Hanafis. The entry on 'Ali al-Razi discusses the layers of muqallids (followers) versus mujtahids, clarifying that even later scholars like Mulla Shams al-Din Ahmad and Abu al-Sa'ud al-'Imadi can be considered among the muqallids capable of tarjih (preference) despite being later in time, because ranks are based on merit, not chronology. Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi's death date is corrected from a common error (884 vs. 482 AH), showing the importance of accurate historiography in fiqh. Qadikhan is praised as 'faqih al-nafs' (innate jurist), indicating his rulings carry greater weight in the school. This glossary therefore not only identifies individuals but also informs the reader about the relative authority of different scholars' opinions within the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
المقلدون (al-muqallidun): Jurists who follow a madhhab and are capable of tarjih (preference) among different rulings, as opposed to absolute mujtahids.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of preferring one opinion over another within the madhhab, a task for qualified muqallids.
المجتهدون (al-mujtahidun): Absolute jurists capable of deriving rulings directly from primary sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the entry of 'Ali al-Razi, who among the following is considered a mujtahid?
A) al-Quduri
B) author of al-Hidayah
C) al-Karkhi
D) 'Ali al-Razi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ranks scholars by their capacity for ijtihad or tarjih; this hierarchy guides which opinions are relied upon in fatwa.

Assessing Scholar Authority: Using Biographical Glossaries in Hanafi Iftaa
Biographical entries with evaluations and death dates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to use a biographical glossary to determine the reliability and weight of a Hanafi scholar's opinions based on death dates, teachers, and assessments.

Core Idea
A scholar's authority in Hanafi fatwa depends not only on their era but on their teachers, students, and explicit evaluations by later authorities.

This lesson examines how biographical details—like death dates, chains of learning, and quality assessments—serve as tools for a mufti to weigh opinions. The entries on Qadikhan and al-Bazdawi show how scholars are evaluated, including corrections of common errors. Understanding these details prevents misattribution of authority.

Guided Path
1
Examine the entry on Qadikhan
Read the biography of Qadikhan. Note his death date (592 AH) and his title 'faqih al-nafs' (innate jurist).
His death date places him in the 6th century AH.
2
Understand the evaluation by later authorities
Kamal Basha considered him from the layer of mujtahids in issues. Qutlubugha said his corrections are preferred because he is 'faqih al-nafs'.
This explicit endorsement raises the weight of his opinions.
3
Examine the entry on al-Bazdawi
Note his birth and death (400-482 AH) and the correction of a mistaken later death date (884 AH).
The correction highlights the importance of accurate historiography.
4
Identify why this matters for iftaa
Accurate death dates help place scholars in the proper tabaqa. A wrong date could misattribute a scholar to a later period, affecting the weight given to their opinions.
A mufti must verify biographical data.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical glossary (الأعلام) of notable Hanafi scholars mentioned in the commentary (Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti). It is typical in classical Hanafi works to include such a section to establish the authority and chain of transmission of the scholars whose views are cited. The entries provide death dates, teachers, students, and sometimes opinions about the scholar's rank. For instance, 'Isam ibn Yusuf is noted for his practice of raising hands in prayer, contrasting with his brother, illustrating differences even among early Hanafis. The entry on 'Ali al-Razi discusses the layers of muqallids (followers) versus mujtahids, clarifying that even later scholars like Mulla Shams al-Din Ahmad and Abu al-Sa'ud al-'Imadi can be considered among the muqallids capable of tarjih (preference) despite being later in time, because ranks are based on merit, not chronology. Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi's death date is corrected from a common error (884 vs. 482 AH), showing the importance of accurate historiography in fiqh. Qadikhan is praised as 'faqih al-nafs' (innate jurist), indicating his rulings carry greater weight in the school. This glossary therefore not only identifies individuals but also informs the reader about the relative authority of different scholars' opinions within the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
فقيه النفس (faqih al-nafs): A jurist with innate understanding of fiqh, whose judgments are considered sound.
طبقة المجتهدين (tabaqat al-mujtahidin): The layer of absolute mujtahids within the Hanafi school.
تصحيح (tashih): The process of correcting or preferring one transmission or opinion over another.

Key Hanafi Scholars and Works: Al-Shurunbulali, Al-Hamawi, and Ibn al-Fasih
Biographical entry listing Hanafi scholars and their works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi scholars and works mentioned in the passage and explain their significance in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Knowing the authors and their works is essential for tracing the transmission of Hanafi rulings.

This passage introduces several key figures in the Hanafi school – al-Shurunbulali, al-Hamawi, and Ibn al-Fasih – and their major works. Understanding these names and their contributions helps you navigate the vast corpus of Hanafi fiqh literature and assess the authority of quoted rulings. Pay close attention to the relationships between the works: commentaries, versifications, and super-commentaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary scholar
Locate the name 'al-Ustadh Hasan ibn Ammar al-Shurunbulali'. Note his famous work, Nur al-Idah, and his title 'al-Ustadh' (the master).
His commentary al-Shurunbulaliyya is a standard text on fiqh.
2
Recognize the associated commentaries
Find the mention of Hashiyat al-Ashbah by al-Hamawi and its commentary Awdaḥ al-Ramz. Understand that these are commentaries on the legal maxims (al-Ashbah) and on the versification (Nazm al-Kanz).
Al-Hamawi's Hashiyah is a key reference for muftis.
3
Note the author of Nazm al-Kanz
Identify Ibn al-Fasih Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hamdani as the author of the poetic work Nazm al-Kanz, also known as Mustahsan al-Tariq. Remember his death date (755 AH).
Nazm al-Kanz versifies Kanz al-Daqaiq, a foundational Hanafi text.
4
Understand the chain of works
Trace the relationship: Nazm al-Kanz is based on Kanz al-Daqaiq (not directly mentioned), and al-Shurunbulali's Nur al-Idah is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. Al-Hamawi's Hashiyah comments on al-Ashbah, which itself is a work on Hanafi legal maxims.
This chain shows the interconnectedness of Hanafi texts.
5
Memorize for future reference
Commit these names, works, and dates to memory. They will appear frequently in advanced fiqh studies and in mufti training.
Use flashcards or a study group to reinforce recall.

الأعلام الوارد ذكرهم في الشرح الأستاذ لحسن بن عمار الشرنبلالي، صاحب نور الإيضاح، كما يظهر من أول الشرنبلالية، وحاشية الأشباه للحموى وشرحه يسمى أوضح الرمز على نظم الكنز. ونظم الكنز : هو لابن الفصيح أحمد بن على الهمداني، واسمه "مستحسن الطريق"، توفى سنة خمس وخمسين وسبعمائة .

And Nazm al-Kanz is by Ibn al-Fasih Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hamdani, and its name is 'Mustahsan al-Tariq', died in the year 755.

The passage provides basic biographical and bibliographical information for reference.

The Authority of Qadikhan's Corrections in Hanafi Fatwa
Biographical entry for Qadikhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the status of Qadikhan's corrections in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy and explain why they are given precedence over others.

Core Idea
Qadikhan's corrections are given precedence because he was a mujtahid in matters and a faqih by nature.

This lesson introduces Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan, a towering figure in the Hanafi school whose corrections are considered superior to others. His biography and the endorsement by later scholars establish his authority in the fatwa process, teaching us how the school ranks its authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and his lineage
Note the full name: Hasan ibn Mansur ibn Mahmud al-Uzjandi al-Farghani, famously known as Qadikhan. His title combines 'qadi' (judge) and 'khan' (ruler), indicating his scholarly and social status.
2
Note his death date and scholarly classification
He died in 592 AH. Kamal Pasha classified him among the 'mujtahidun fil-masa'il' – those capable of weighing and preferring opinions within the Hanafi school, not independent mujtahids.
Mujtahid fil-masa'il is a later category of jurists who specialize in tarjih (preference) among existing rulings.
3
Understand Qasim ibn Qutlubugha's statement
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha said: 'What Qadikhan corrects is given precedence over the correction of others, because he is a faqih by nature.' This indicates his innate juristic insight (faqih al-nafs).
This statement establishes a hierarchical principle: not all corrections are equal; those of a 'faqih by nature' are authoritative.
4
Reflect on the implication for fatwa hierarchy
The passage shows that later Hanafi masters recognized Qadikhan's superior ability to correct and prefer rulings. In practice, a mufti should rely on Qadikhan's fatwa when it conflicts with lesser authorities.
This is an example of tarjih bil-a'aliyya (preference by personal expertise) rather than merely chronological precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فخر الدین قاضيخان : هو حسن بن منصور بن محمود الأوز جندى الفرغاني المشهور بقاضيخان و أوزجند" : مدينة بنواحي "أصبهان" بقرب "فرغانة". توفى ليلة الاثنين سنة ٥٩٢هـ . عده كمال باشا من طبقة المجتهدين في المسائل. وقال قاسم ابن قطلوبغا في تصحيح القدورى " : "ما يصححه قاضيخان مقدم على تصحيح غيره ؛ لأنه فقيه النفس".
Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan: He is Hasan ibn Mansur ibn Mahmud al-Uzjandi al-Farghani, famous as Qadikhan. And Uzjand is a town in the region of Isfahan near Farghana. He died on Monday night in the year 592 AH. Kamal Pasha counted him among the mujtahidun in matters. And Qasim ibn Qutlubugha said in his correction of al-Quduri: 'What Qadikhan corrects is given precedence over the correction of others, because he is a fagih by nature.'
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This entry gives biographical details of Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan, a leading Hanafi jurist known for his authoritative corrections. His death date is 592 AH. Kamal Pasha considered him a mujtahid, and Qasim ibn Qutlubugha emphasized the precedence of his corrections over others due to his deep juristic insight.

Key Terms
قاضيخان (Qadikhan): Title meaning 'judge' (qadi) plus 'khan', used for Hasan ibn Mansur, a Hanafi jurist
مجتهد في المسائل (mujtahid fil-masa'il): A jurist who has the ability to weigh and prefer opinions within the Hanafi school, as opposed to an independent mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because he is older
B) Because he is a faqih by nature
C) Because he wrote more books
D) Because he was a qadi

Key Takeaway
Qadikhan's corrections are given precedence in Hanafi fatwa because he was recognized as a mujtahid fil-masa'il and a deep jurist (faqih by nature).

Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi: A Corrected Biography
Biographical notice with date correction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct nisba, full name, and death date of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and identify the source of a common historical error.

Core Idea
Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi died in 482 AH, not 884 AH – a common error from misreading biographical indexes.

Knowing a scholar's correct biography is essential for evaluating the weight of their rulings. This lesson establishes the birth and death dates of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, a key Hanafi usuli and jurist, and corrects a widespread mistake in later sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisba and its origin
The nisba 'al-Bazdawi' refers to the fortress Bazdah near Nasaf in Transoxiana. Understand how geographical attribution is formed in classical Islamic scholarship.
2
Memorize the full name and death date
His full name is Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Musa. He died on 5th Rajab 482 AH, and his coffin was taken to Samarkand.
The year 482 AH is approximately 1089 CE.
3
Recognize the common error
Mawlana Abd al-Hayy notes that some later authors erroneously record his death as 884 AH, a mistake arising from following the author of Kashf (likely Haji Khalifa's Kashf al-Zunun).
The error is a gross miscalculation of several centuries.
4
Verify with additional sources
Cross-reference with reliable bio-bibliographical works. The text also refers to Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Fakhr al-Islam and Fihris al-Kutub.
Always check multiple primary sources for biographical data.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فخر الإسلام البزدوى : هى نسبة إلى "بزده" (بالفتح ثم السكون وفتح الدال المهملة آخره (هاء) ويقال بزدوة، والنسبة بزدوی و بزدی ، قلعة حصينة على ستة فراسخ من "نسف" ، كذا في معجم البلدان. و البزدوي " : هو على بن محمد ابن الحسين بن عبد الكريم بن موسى، ولد في حدود سنة أربعمائة، ومات في خامس رجب سنة اثنين وثمانين وأربعمائة ، وحمل تابوته إلى "سمرقند" . قال مولانا عبدالحی : قد أرخ بعض معاصرينا في كتابه الحطة وفاته سنة أربع وثمانين وثمان مائة، وهو خطأ فاحش صدر من تقليد صاحب الكشف، فإنه أرخ عند ذكر شراح جامع البخاري كذلك . راجع أيضا "شرح الجامع الصغير لفخر الإسلام في فهرس الكتب .
Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi: It is a nisba to 'Bazdah' (with fatha then sukun and fatha of the important dal, its end is ha) and it is said Bazdawah, and the nisba is Bazdawi and Bazdi, a strong fortress six farsakhs from Nasaf, as in Mu'jam al-Buldan. And al-Bazdawi is Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Musa, born around 400 AH, died on 5th Rajab 482 AH, and his coffin was carried to Samarkand. Mawlana Abd al-Hayy said: One of our contemporaries dated his death in his book al-Hitta as 884 AH, and it is a gross error arising from following the author of Kashf, for he dated when mentioning the commentators of Sahih al-Bukhari likewise. See also Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Fakhr al-Islam in Fihris al-Kutub.

Commentary
This entry provides biographical details of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, a prominent Hanafi scholar. It gives the origin of his nisba, his full name, birth and death dates, and a refutation of an erroneous death date given by some later authors. The correct death date is 482 AH, not 884 AH as mistakenly recorded.

Key Terms
البزدوى (al-Bazdawi): Attribution to Bazdah, a fortress near Nasaf in Transoxiana
فخر الإسلام (Fakhr al-Islam): Title meaning 'Pride of Islam', honorific for al-Bazdawi

Key Terms from Source Passage

Qasim ibn Qutlubugha: A Hanafi Scholar's Biography
Biographical entry for Qasim ibn Qutlubugha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical facts of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha and explain their significance for evaluating his authority in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, student of Ibn al-Humam, died 829 AH — a later authority whose opinion carries weight in the Hanafi school.

This lesson presents the biography of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, a Hanafi scholar of the 9th century AH. Understanding his life, teachers, and scholarly standing helps muftis assess the reliability of his legal opinions. The passage also corrects a common error in his death year, reinforcing the importance of accurate historical knowledge for fatwa work.

Guided Path
1
Identify birth and death years
Locate the exact birth year (802 AH) and death year (829 AH) in the text. Note that both are in Cairo.
The birth year is clearly given; the death year is specified on the 4th of Rabi' al-Akhir.
2
Identify his primary teacher
Find the name of the scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha closely accompanied: Ibn al-Humam. Note the phrase 'اشتدت عنايته بملازمة ابن الهمام'.
Ibn al-Humam is a major Hanafi authority; being his student positions Qasim as a later mutakkhir.
3
Assess his scholarly qualities
List the qualities mentioned: imam, allama, broad knowledge of the madhhab, eloquent, able to debate. These indicate his competence as a mufti.
The text says he was 'متقدماً في هذا الفن' – advanced in this art (likely usul or fiqh).
4
Correct the mistaken death year
Note the erroneous death year of 369 AH in al-Kashf. Understand why it is impossible (would predate his teacher Ibn al-Humam).
This correction demonstrates the need for chronological accuracy in assessing a scholar's place.
5
Summarize his place in the fatwa hierarchy
As a student of Ibn al-Humam and a 9th-century authority, Qasim ibn Qutlubugha belongs to the mutakhkhirun period. His opinions are part of the later Hanafi corpus but must be weighed against earlier authorities.
The mufta bihi is typically from the mutakhkhirin, but his teacher Ibn al-Humam is more central.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاسم بن قطلوبغا : هو أبو العدل زين الدين قاسم بن قطلوبغا الحنفى، ولد سنة ٨٠٢هـ بالقاهرة. و مات أبوه (وهو صغير) فحفظ القرآن وكتبا فعرضها على العز بن جماعة، وتكسب مدة بالخياطة، ثم أقبل على الاشتغال، واشتدت عنايته بملازمة ابن الهمام بحيث سمع عليه غالب ما كان يقرأ عنده، وكان إمامًا، علامة، قوى المشاركة في فنون واسع الباع في استحضار مذهبه متقدماً في هذا الفن، طلق اللسان، قادراً على المناظرة وإفحام الخصم. وكانت وفاته بحارة الديلم رابع ربيع الآخر سنة ٨٢٩هـ ، كذا ذكر في التعليقات السنية نقلا عن السخاوي. وما في الكشف عند ذكر مختصر القدوري : " من أنه توفي سنة ٣٦٩هـ فهو زلة قلم أو تصحيف من الكاتب ؛ لأنه يقتضي التقدم على ابن الهمام مع أنه تلميذه، ليس بمقدم عليه كما لا يخفى .
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha: He is Abu al-Adl Zayn al-Din Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi, born in the year 802 AH in Cairo. His father died while he was young, so he memorized the Quran and books and presented them to al-Izz ibn Jama'a. He earned a living for a while by tailoring, then turned to study, and his attention intensified in accompanying Ibn al-Humam such that he heard most of what he read with him. He was an imam, a scholar, strong in participation in various fields, broad in knowledge of his madhhab, advanced in this art, eloquent, able to debate and silence opponents. He died in Harat al-Daylam on the 4th of Rabi' al-Akhir 829 AH, as mentioned in al-Ta'liqat al-Sunniyya quoting al-Sakhawi. And what is in al-Kashf when mentioning Mukhtasar al-Quduri that he died in 369 AH is a slip of the pen or scribal error, because it would place him before Ibn al-Humam whereas he is his student, not preceding him, as is obvious.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This entry details the life of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, a Hanafi scholar born in Cairo. It describes his early hardships, his devotion to studying under Ibn al-Humam, and his scholarly qualities. His correct death date is 829 AH, and a mistaken earlier date in al-Kashf is refuted.

Key Terms
ابن الهمام (Ibn al-Humam): Reference to the teacher of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, a major Hanafi scholar

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Ibn al-Humam
C) Al-Sakhawi
D) Al-Quduri

Key Takeaway
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, a student of Ibn al-Humam and a scholar of the 9th century AH, holds a respected place in the Hanafi mutakhkhirun, and his correct death year of 829 AH is vital for accurate historical placement.

Cross-Madhhab References in Hanafi Fatwa Literature: The Case of al-Qadi Husayn
Biographical entry of a Shafi'i jurist in a Hanafi fatwa manual

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a Hanafi usul al-iftaa text includes a biographical entry for a Shafi'i scholar and identify the significance of cross-madhhab references in the Hanafi fatwa tradition.

Core Idea
Hanafi muftis reference Shafi'i scholars like al-Qadi Husayn to enrich fatwa methodology, not to adopt their rulings.

Even in a work devoted to Hanafi fatwa methodology, we find a biography of a Shafi'i jurist. This is not accidental. The inclusion of al-Qadi Husayn al-Marwazi highlights the Hanafi tradition's engagement with other madhhabs. In this lesson, we will explore why a Hanafi commentator would introduce such a figure and what it teaches us about the breadth of sources a mufti may consult.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scholar's Madhhab and Role
Read the passage to determine al-Qadi Husayn's madhhab (Shafi'i) and his reputation (great imam, author of al-Ta'liqa, teacher, judge). Why would a Hanafi text feature a non-Hanafi scholar?
The phrase 'al-Shafi'i' is explicit.
2
Analyze the Context of the Reference
Consider that the source is a Sharh on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti', a Hanafi work on fatwa methodology. Biographical entries here often serve to acknowledge authoritative figures whose works or opinions are cited in fatwa literature, even if from other madhhabs.
3
Explain the Significance for Hanafi Fatwa Methodology
Cross-madhhab references demonstrate that a mufti should be aware of scholarly consensus and disagreement. Citing a Shafi'i scholar shows comprehensive knowledge, which is valued in iftaa.
This does not imply the Hanafi school adopts Shafi'i rulings; it merely recognizes the scholar's stature.
4
Draw a Practical Lesson for Modern Fatwa Practice
A contemporary Hanafi mufti may refer to works of other madhhabs for comparison, but the operative ruling (mufta bihi) remains from the Hanafi school. The entry reminds us that authoritative fatwa requires awareness of broader scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القاضي حسين : هو أبو على الحسين بن محمد بن أحمد المروزي الفقيه، الشافعي، المعروف بالقاضي، صاحب التعليقة في الفقه كان إماماً كبيراً، صاحب وجوه غريبة في المذهب. أخذ الفقه عن أبي بكر القفال المروزي، وصنف في الأصول، والفروع والخلاف. ولم يزل يحكم بين الناس ويدرس ويفتى. وأخذ عنه الفقه جماعة من الأعيان منهم : أبو محمد الحسين بن مسعود الفراء البغوى، صاحب کتاب التهذيب وغيره، وتوفى سنة اثنتين وستين وأربعمائة بمرو.
Al-Qadi Husayn: He is Abu Ali al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Marwazi, the jurist, the Shafi'i, known as al-Qadi, author of al-Ta'liqa in fiqh. He was a great imam, possessor of strange aspects in the madhhab. He took fiqh from Abu Bakr al-Qaffal al-Marwazi, and wrote works in usul, furu', and khilaf. He continued to judge among people, teach, and give fatwas. A group of eminent persons took fiqh from him, among them: Abu Muhammad al-Husayn ibn Mas'ud al-Farra' al-Baghawi, author of Kitab al-Tahdhib and others. He died in the year 462 AH in Marw.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This entry provides a biography of al-Qadi Husayn, a Shafi'i scholar. Despite being from a different madhhab, he is noted in the Hanafi commentary due to his influence. His death date is 462 AH. He was a teacher of al-Baghawi, the famous mufassir and muhaddith.

Key Terms
التعليقة (al-Ta'liqa): A work in fiqh by al-Qadi Husayn, likely a commentary or gloss

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Maliki
C) Shafi'i
D) Hanbali

Key Takeaway
The inclusion of a Shafi'i scholar like al-Qadi Husayn in a Hanafi fatwa manual underscores the importance of cross-madhhab knowledge, but does not alter the Hanafi school's own methodology or authority.
