Al-Hariri: Commentator of al-Hidayah and Refuter of Istibdal
Biographical entry for a Hanafi jurist and author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of al-Hariri and explain how his authority as a judge and commentator strengthens his work in Hanafi iftaa.

Core Idea
A scholar's authority in iftaa is built on lineage, teachers, judicial role, and mastery of core texts.

This lesson introduces you to Shams al-Din al-Hariri, a towering figure in the Hanafi madhhab. His commentary on al-Hidayah and his treatise against istibdal (exchange of waqf properties) are still referenced by muftis today. Understanding his background helps you appreciate the weight of his opinions in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's full identity
Find al-Hariri's full name, kunya, birth, and death dates from the text. Note the sources cited (al-Kashf, al-Fawa'id, Husn al-Muhadara).
All sources agree on death year 728 AH, birth 653 AH.
2
Trace his scholarly lineage
Identify his teachers (Ibn al-Mu'allim Isma'il al-Qurashi) and his own students. This chain connects him to earlier Hanafi authorities.
His teacher studied under Jamal Mahmud al-Husayri, linking to earlier generations.
3
Identify his major work
Note the title 'Idah al-Istidlal 'ala Ibtal al-Istibdal' and its subject: refuting the exchange of endowment properties. This is a fatwa-related work.
The title itself indicates the method (istidlal) and the issue (istibdal).
4
Understand his authority
Al-Hariri was a chief judge (qadi al-qudat) in Damascus and Egypt and a commentator of al-Hidayah. These roles establish his expertise and reliability.
Commentary on al-Hidayah requires deep mastery of Hanafi fiqh.
5
Connect to iftaa
Assess how al-Hariri's credentials affect the weight of his rulings. A mufti would give preference to a scholar with such credentials when conflicting opinions exist.
His work on istibdal is a direct contribution to fatwa literature on waqf.

Source Text

Ibn Nujaym and al-Bahr al-Raiq
Biographical note identifying author and work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Nujaym and state the relationship between al-Bahr al-Raiq and Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Core Idea
Al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, not an independent work.

This lesson introduces a key figure in the later Hanafi school: Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym (d. 970 AH). His commentary al-Bahr al-Raiq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq is a cornerstone text for fatwa and fiqh analysis. Understanding its place in the Hanafi literary tradition is essential for grasping how later jurists built upon earlier manuals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author
Note the full name and death date of Ibn Nujaym, as given in the source. He is a late Hanafi authority from Egypt.
His death year (970 AH) places him in the 10th Islamic century.
2
Identify the work
Al-Bahr al-Raiq is a sharh (commentary). Recognize that its structure follows the matn (base text) it explains.
The base text is Kanz al-Daqa'iq, a famous Hanafi manual by Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi (d. 710 AH).
3
Determine the relationship
The Arabic 'شرح كنز الدقائق' explicitly states al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary. Understand that a sharh expounds on the matn's rulings, proofs, and disputes.
Many later Hanafi fatwa collections rely on al-Bahr al-Raiq for tarjih (preferred opinions).
4
Assess its significance in iftaa
Ibn Nujaym's work is frequently cited in fatwa literature. Recognize it as a source for the mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school.
It is considered a reliable reference for the later fatwa methodology.

Source Text

11 - al-Bahr: It is al-Bahr al-Raiq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq in Hanafi branches (furu'), by the Imam the eminent scholar Shaykh Zayn al-Din ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad known as Ibn Nujaym al-Misri al-Hanafi, died in 970 AH.

Key Terms
ابن نجيم (Ibn Nujaym): Zayn al-Din ibn Ibrahim ibn Muhammad, known as Ibn Nujaym, a Hanafi jurist and author of al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Al-Kasani and His Work Badai' al-Sanai'
Biographical entry on al-Kasani and his work Badai' al-Sanai'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of al-Kasani and explain how his work Badai' al-Sanai' became a foundational reference for Hanafi fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Al-Kasani's unmatched commentary won him a scholar-wife and secured his work as a pillar of Hanafi fatwa.

This lesson introduces you to one of the most celebrated Hanafi jurists, Ala' al-Din al-Kasani, and his magnum opus, Badai' al-Sanai'. Understanding the lives of our great imams and the stature of their works deepens our appreciation of the fiqh tradition and its transmission. As a future mufti, knowing which texts to rely on and why is essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author
Read the biographical details: his full name, nisba, title (Malik al-'Ulama'), and death date (587 AH/1191 CE).
The nisba may be al-Kasani or al-Kashani; both are found.
2
Map His Scholarly Chain
Note his teachers (al-Samarqandi, al-Bazdawi, al-Mak-hul, al-Sarakhsi) and his students (his son Mahmud, al-Ghaznawi).
This chain connects him to the earlier Hanafi authorities.
3
Understand the Marriage Story
Al-Kasani married his teacher's daughter Fatima after presenting his commentary. Fatima was a scholar who co-signed fatwas with her father and husband.
This highlights the high scholarly status of the family and the work.
4
Appreciate the Work's Significance
Badai' al-Sanai' is a commentary on Tuhfat al-Fuqaha. Ibn Abidin praised it as unparalleled. It is a key reference for Hanafi fatwa.
The work's name means 'wonders of the crafts' – indicating its systematic arrangement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٢ - البدائع : لعلاء الدين مسعود بن أحمد الكاساني، هو شرح عظيم لـ"تحفة الفقهاء فى ثلاث مجلدات و تمام اسمه بدائع الصنائع في ترتيب الشرائع" وهو تأليف يطابق اسمه معناه كذا في الكشف. وفيه تصريح بأنه في ثلاث مجلدات، لكنه طبع بمصر في سبع مجلدات سنة ۲۷ - ۱۳۲۸هـ . . . وقال ابن عابدين في رد المحتار: "هذا الكتاب جليل الشأن، لم أرَ له نظيراً في كتبنا وهو للإمام أبي بكر بن مسعود بن أحمد، الكاسانی، شرح به "تحفة الفقهاء الشيخه علاء الدين السمرقندی، فلما عرضه عليه، زوجه ابنته فاطمة بعد ما خطبها الملوك من أبيها ، فامتنع ، وكانت الفتوى تخرج من دارهم وعليها خطها وخط أبيها وزوجها". ثم اعلم أن أبا بكر بن مسعود بن أحمد علاء الدين الكاساني، ملك العلماء، أخذ العلم عن علاء الدين السمر قندى صاحب التحفة عن صدر الإسلام أبي اليسر البزدوى، وعن أبي المعين ميمون المكحول، وعن مجد الأئمة السرخكى، وله كتاب " السلطان المبين في أصول الدين". وتفقه عليه ابنه محمود، وأحمد بن محمود الغزنوي، صاحب المقدمة الغزنوية، مات في عاشر رجب سنة سبع وثمانين وخمسمائة، ودفن بظاهر حلب عند قبر زوجته فاطمة ابنة صاحب التحفة الفقيهة العالمة . والدعاء عند قبرهما مستجاب . ونسبته إلى الكاسان (بالكاف ثم الألف ثم السين المهملة فألف ثم النون بلدة وراء الشام ذكره السمعاني. وقد يقال في نسبته : الكاشاني (بالمعجمة بدل المهملة وفى مشتبه النسبة للذهبي: "قاسان بلد كبير بتركستان وأهلها يقولون : "كاسان" . وكانت من محاسن الدنيا، خربت باستيلاء الترك عليها، ومنها العلامة علاء الدين الكاساني من أئمة الحنفية بدمشق أيام الملك نور الدين .
12 - al-Bada'i': by Ala' al-Din Mas'ud ibn Ahmad al-Kasani, it is a great commentary on 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' in three volumes, and its full name is 'Badai' al-Sanai' fi Tartib al-Shara'i'' and it is a work whose name matches its meaning as stated in al-Kashf. In it is an explicit statement that it is in three volumes, but it was printed in Egypt in seven volumes in 1327-1328 AH. Ibn Abidin said in Radd al-Muhtar: 'This book is of great importance, I have not seen its like in our books, and it is by Imam Abu Bakr ibn Mas'ud ibn Ahmad al-Kasani. He commented on 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' by his teacher Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi. When he presented it to him, he married him to his daughter Fatima after kings had asked for her hand from her father, but he refused. Fatwas would issue from their house with her signature, her father's signature, and her husband's signature.' Then know that Abu Bakr ibn Mas'ud ibn Ahmad Ala' al-Din al-Kasani, the king of scholars, took knowledge from Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi (author of al-Tuhfa) from Sadr al-Islam Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi, and from Abu al-Mu'in Maymun al-Mak-hul, and from Majd al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. He has the book 'al-Sultan al-Mubin fi Usul al-Din'. His son Mahmud studied fiqh under him, and Ahmad ibn Mahmud al-Ghaznawi, author of al-Muqaddima al-Ghaznawiyya. He died on the 10th of Rajab 587 AH, and was buried outside Aleppo near the grave of his wife Fatima, the daughter of the author of al-Tuhfa, a jurist and scholar. Supplication at their graves is answered. His nisba is to Kasan (with kaf, then alif, then sin, then alif, then nun – a town beyond Syria, mentioned by al-Sam'ani. It is also said in his nisba: al-Kashani (with a dotted letter instead of the undotted). And in Mushtabih al-Nisba by al-Dhahabi: 'Qasan is a large city in Turkestan, its inhabitants say Kasan. It was one of the beauties of the world, destroyed by the Turkish invasion. From it is the scholar Ala' al-Din al-Kasani, one of the imams of the Hanafis in Damascus during the reign of King Nur al-Din.'
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This is a comprehensive biographical entry on Ala' al-Din al-Kasani (d. 587 AH), a giant of the Hanafi school. His monumental commentary 'Badai' al-Sanai'' on his teacher's work 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' is praised by Ibn Abidin. The text recounts the famous story of al-Kasani marrying his teacher's daughter Fatima after presenting his commentary, and she was herself a scholar who co-signed fatwas. The entry details his teachers, students, and the correct nisba (Kasan or Kashan), providing geographical and historical notes.

Key Terms
بدائع الصنائع (Badai' al-Sanai'): Al-Kasani's commentary on Tuhfat al-Fuqaha, a major Hanafi fiqh work arranged by chapters.
الكاساني (al-Kasani): Ala' al-Din Abu Bakr ibn Mas'ud al-Kasani, a leading Hanafi jurist known as 'king of scholars' (malik al-ulama).

Al-Marghinani and His Works: Bidaya and Hidaya
Biographical entry on al-Marghinani's works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the relationship between al-Marghinani's Bidayat al-Mubtadi and al-Hidayah, and identify the two source texts combined in the Bidaya.

Core Idea
Al-Hidayah is the commentary on al-Marghinani's own Bidaya, which merges Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.

This lesson introduces the foundational Hanafi text 'al-Hidayah' and its author, al-Marghinani. You will learn that al-Hidayah is not an independent work but a commentary on his own 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi', which itself synthesizes two earlier authoritative texts. Understanding this textual lineage is key to appreciating the Hidayah's structure and authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his era
Who is al-Marghinani? Note his full name, death year (593 AH), and his role as a Hanafi jurist.
2
Recognize the base text
The Bidaya is a concise fiqh work. Its full title is 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi fi al-Furu'. It is a summary combining two earlier works.
3
Identify the two source texts
Al-Marghinani combined 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' by Imam al-Quduri and 'al-Jami' al-Saghir' by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Note the arrangement follows al-Jami' al-Saghir.
4
Link the Bidaya to its commentary
Al-Marghinani wrote a commentary on his own Bidaya, initially intending to call it 'Kifayat al-Muntaha', but it became known as 'al-Hidayah'. This commentary is the famous work used worldwide.
5
Appreciate the significance
The Hidayah is one of the most important Hanafi fiqh books. Knowing its origins helps you understand its development and authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٣ - البداية : بداية المبتدئ في الفروع للشيخ الإمام أبي الحسن على بن أبى بكر المرغینانی، شرحه في كتاب الهداية" ، توفى سنة ٥٩٣هـ . وهى مختصر أولها: " الحمد لله الذي هدانا إلى بالغ حكمته ... إلخ . ذكر فيه : أنه جمع بين "مختصر القدورى" و "الجامع الصغير". واختار بترتيب الجامع الصغير " تبركا بما اختاره محمد ابن الحسن قال : ولو وفقت لشرحه أرسمه بـ "كفاية المنتهى " .
13 - al-Bidaya: Bidayat al-Mubtadi fi al-Furu' by the Shaykh Imam Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Abi Bakr al-Marghinani, he commented on it in the book 'al-Hidayah', died in 593 AH. It is a summary whose opening is: 'Praise be to Allah who guided us to the perfection of His wisdom... etc.' He mentioned in it that he combined 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' and 'al-Jami' al-Saghir'. And he chose the arrangement of al-Jami' al-Saghir, seeking blessing from what Muhammad ibn al-Hasan chose. He said: 'If I am granted success in commenting on it, I will name it "Kifayat al-Muntaha".'
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This entry introduces Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH), the author of the seminal Hanafi work 'al-Hidayah', which is a commentary on his own text 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi'. The 'Bidaya' itself is a concise work combining two earlier authoritative texts: 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' and 'al-Jami' al-Saghir' by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Al-Marghinani followed the arrangement of 'al-Jami' al-Saghir' for blessings. He originally intended to name his commentary 'Kifayat al-Muntaha' but eventually it became known as 'al-Hidayah'.

Key Terms
بداية المبتدئ (Bidayat al-Mubtadi): A concise Hanafi fiqh text by al-Marghinani that combines Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.
الهداية (al-Hidayah): The famous commentary by al-Marghinani on his own Bidayat al-Mubtadi, one of the most important works in Hanafi fiqh.
كفاية المنتهى (Kifayat al-Muntaha): The original title al-Marghinani intended for his commentary on the Bidaya, later known as al-Hidayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir
C) al-Hidayah and al-Jami' al-Saghir
D) al-Hidayah and Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Key Takeaway
Al-Hidayah is a commentary on al-Marghinani's Bidayat al-Mubtadi, which itself synthesizes Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Al-Hakim al-Naysaburi: a hadith master whose works inform the Hanafi mufti's search for authoritative narrations.

This passage introduces al-Hakim al-Naysaburi, a towering hadith scholar whose works like al-Mustadrak are essential references in Hanafi fiqh and usul al-iftā. الكتب الواردة في الشرح الحاكم النيسابوري، ثم طلب الحديث و غلب عليه فاشتهر به وسمع من جماعة لا يحصون كثرة، فإن معجم شيوخه يقرب من ألفى رجل، حتى روى عمن عاش بعده؛ السعة روايته وكثرة شيوخه، وصنف فى علومه ما يبلغ ألفا وخمسمائة جزء. وله إلى الحجاز والعراق رحلتان، وكانت الرحلة الثانية سنة ٣٦٠هـ، وناظر الحفاظ، وذكر الشيوخ وكتب عنهم أيضاً، وباحث الدارقطني فرضيه وتقلد القضاء بنيسابور في سنة تسع وخمسين وثلاث مائة ٣٥٣هـ في أيام الدولة السامانية، ووزارة أبي النصر محمد ابن عبد الجبار القبتي وقلد بعد ذلك قضاء جرجان فامتنع، وكانوا ينفذونه في الرسائل إلى ملوك بني بويه. وكانت ولادته سنة ٣٢١هـ بنيسابور، وتوفى بها يوم الثلاثاء، ثالث صفر سنة ٤٠٥هـ. وقال الجيلى فى كتاب الإرشاد: توفى سنة ٤٠٣هـ، وسمع الحديث في سنة ٣٠، وأملى بما وراء النهر سنة ٥٥، وبالعراق سنة سبع وستين ٦٧. ولازمه الدارقطني، وسمع منه أبو بكر القفال والشاشي و أنظارها. وإنما عرف بالحاكم لتقلده القضاء. ومن أشهر كتبه: المستدرك على الصحيحين مطبوع في أربع مجلدات. ومن كتبه المطبوعة معرفة علوم الحديث و المدخل. وأما تاريخ نيسابور وغيره من الكتب الكثيرة له، لم تطبع حتى الآن.
The books included in the commentary: al-Hakim al-Naysaburi. Then he sought hadith and it overcame him, so he became famous for it. He heard from countless people; the dictionary of his teachers approaches two thousand men, such that he narrated from those who lived after him due to the breadth of his narrations and the abundance of his teachers. He authored in his sciences what amounts to one thousand five hundred parts. He made two journeys to the Hijaz and Iraq, the second journey in the year 360 AH. He debated the memorizers, mentioned the teachers, and wrote from them as well. He debated al-Daraqutni and was appointed as judge in Nishapur in the year 359 AH during the Samanid state and the vizierate of Abu Nasr Muhammad ibn Abd al-Jabbar al-Qabti. After that, he was appointed as judge of Jurjan but declined. They would send him in messages to the kings of the Buwayhids. His birth was in 321 AH in Nishapur, and he died there on Tuesday, the third of Safar 405 AH. Al-Jili said in Kitab al-Irshad that he died in 403 AH. He heard hadith in the year 30, dictated in Transoxiana in the year 55, and in Iraq in the year 67. Al-Daraqutni accompanied him, and Abu Bakr al-Qaffal and al-Shashi and their likes heard from him. He was known as al-Hakim because of his assumption of judgeship. Among his most famous books: al-Mustadrak 'ala al-Sahihayn, printed in four volumes. Among his printed books: Ma'rifat 'Ulum al-Hadith and al-Madkhal. As for Tarikh Nisabur and other many books of his, they have not been printed until now.

The text details his extensive travel, his vast number of teachers, his judicial appointments, and his major works. It emphasizes his prolific output – 1,500 parts – and his fame as a narrator. The entry corrects common details about his death year and lists his printed and unprinted works. As front matter in a Hanafi usul al-iftā commentary, this biography serves to identify one of the authoritative sources referenced in the work.

Key Terms

Jami' al-Fuslayn and Its Author Ibn Qadi Samawa
Describing the book Jami' al-Fuslayn and biography of its author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the book Jami' al-Fuslayn and its author, and explain why it is a key reference for Hanafi muftis.

Core Idea
Jami' al-Fuslayn is a foundational Hanafi text on transactions, compiled by a scholar who studied with the giants of his age.

This passage introduces us to Ibn Qadi Samawa and his famous work Jami' al-Fuslayn, a book that combines two earlier Fusul works. Knowing the authors and lineages of our key texts helps us understand their authority and scope. Here we learn why this book is trusted by judges and muftis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book
What is Jami' al-Fuslayn? What two works does it combine, and what is its subject matter?
It combines Fusul al-'Imadi and Fusul al-Isturushni, focusing on mu'amalat (transactions).
2
Locate the author
Who is Ibn Qadi Samawa? Note his full name, birth, death, and key biographical details.
Badr al-Din Mahmud, born in Samawa, died c. 818/823 AH.
3
Trace the scholarly lineage
Who were his teachers? This establishes the chain of knowledge transmission.
Studied under al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani and Akmal al-Din al-Babarti.
4
Assess the book's authority
Why is Jami' al-Fuslayn considered mu'tabar (reliable) and used by judges and muftis?
Due to its comprehensive coverage of transactions and the author's deep scholarship.
5
Note the textual variants
What discrepancies exist between sources regarding the author's father's name and death year?
Al-Kashf gives father as Isma'il and death 823; Tarab al-Amathil gives Isra'il and death 818.

-۲۳ جامع الفصولين : قال الشامي : هو كتاب معتبر لابن قاضي سماوة، جمع فيه بين فصول العمادي وفصول الإستروشني . وفي الكشف : جامع الفصولين في الفروع مجلد للشيخ بدر الدين محمود بن إسماعيل الشهير بابن قاضي سماوة، الحنفي، المتوفى سنة ثلاث وعشرين وثمانمائة، وهو كتاب مشهور متداول في أيدى الحكام والمفتين ؛ لكونه في المعاملات خاصة جمع فيه بين فصول العمادي وفصول الإستروشنى، وأحاط وأجاد أوله الحمد لله الذى أعلى شأن الشريعة ... إلخ" . وفيه أيضا بعد أسطر : "أنه شرع في تأليفه في جمادى الأولى من شهور سنة اثنتى عشرة وثمانمائة، وختمه في صفر سنة أربع عشرة وثمانمائة " . انتهى . وذكر ترجمته في طرب الأماثل بما لفظه : الشيخ بدر الدين محمود بن إسرائيل ابن عبد العزيز الشهير بابن قاضى سماوة، ولد في قلعة سماوة من بلاد الروم حين كان أبوه قاضياً بها، وكان أيضاً أمير العسكر بها ، وكان فتح تلك القلعة أيضا بيده. وأخذ العلم في صباه عن والده وحفظ القرآن وقرأ بقونية من بلاد الروم بعضاً من العلوم وعلم النجوم على مولانا فيض الله من تلامذة ،مولا فضل ومكث أربعة أشهر. ولما توفى مولانا فیض الله ارتحل إلى الديار المصرية، وقرأ هنالك مع السيد الشريف الجرجاني على مبارك شاه المنطقى المدرس بالقاهرة، وقرأ مع السيد على أكمل الدين البابرتي، وبرع في جميع العلوم. و له تصانيف كثيرة منها : لطائف الإشارات في الفقه " و جامع الفصولين و عنقود الجواهر شرح كتاب المقصود في الصرف"، وكانت وفاته سنة ۸۱٨ تقريبا ومن شركاءه في درسه المولى العالم الحاج باشاه، صاحب کتاب الشفاء والتسهيل في الطب" ، و حواشی شرح المطالع" و "شرح الطوالع وكان السيد الشريف يشهد لهما بالفضيلة كذا فى الشقائق النعمانية. وهو مخالف لما ذكره صاحب الكشف في اسم أبيه وسنة وفاته فافهم.
23. Jami' al-Fuslayn: al-Shami said: It is a reliable book by Ibn Qadi Samawa, in which he combined Fusul al-'Imadi and Fusul al-Isturushni. And in al-Kashf: Jami' al-Fuslayn on branches is a volume by Shaykh Badr al-Din Mahmud ibn Isma'il, known as Ibn Qadi Samawa, the Hanafi, who died in 823 AH, and it is a famous book circulated among judges and muftis, because it concerns transactions; he combined Fusul al-'Imadi and Fusul al-Isturushni, and encompassed and excelled. Its beginning: 'Alhamdulillah who elevated the status of Shari'ah...' etc. And in it also after lines: 'He began composing it in Jumada al-Ula of 812 AH and finished it in Safar 814 AH.' End. And he mentioned his biography in Tarab al-Amathil with the wording: Shaykh Badr al-Din Mahmud ibn Isra'il ibn Abd al-Aziz, known as Ibn Qadi Samawa, born in the fortress of Samawa in the land of Rum when his father was a judge there, and he was also the commander of the army there, and the conquest of that fortress was also by his hand. He acquired knowledge in his youth from his father, memorized the Quran, and read in Quniyah in the land of Rum some of the sciences and astrology under Mawlana Fayd Allah, from the students of Mawla Fadl, and he stayed four months. When Mawlana Fayd Allah died, he traveled to Egypt, and there he studied with al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani under Mubarak Shah al-Mantiqi the teacher in Cairo, and studied with al-Sayyid 'Ali Akmal al-Din al-Babarti, and excelled in all sciences. He has many works, including: Lata'if al-Isharat in fiqh, Jami' al-Fuslayn, and 'Unqud al-Jawahir, commentary on al-Maqsud in morphology. His death was around 818 AH. Among his study companions was the scholar al-Hajj Pasha, author of al-Shifa' wa al-Tashil fi al-Tibb, and commentaries on Sharh al-Matali' and Sharh al-Tawali'. Al-Sayyid al-Sharif testified to their virtue, as in al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya. And it differs from what the author of al-Kashf mentioned regarding his father's name and year of death, so understand.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed description of the book 'Jami' al-Fuslayn' and its author Ibn Qadi Samawa. It begins by quoting al-Shami describing it as a reliable book that combines two earlier works: Fusul al-'Imadi and Fusul al-Isturushni. Then from al-Kashf, it gives the full title, the author's name, death date, and notes its popularity among judges and muftis because it covers transactions. It also mentions when the author started and finished writing. The passage then provides a biography of the author, including his birthplace, education, teachers, travels to Egypt, studies with al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani and others, his students, and his death date. It notes a discrepancy regarding his father's name and death year between sources.

Key Terms
جامع الفصولين (Jami' al-Fuslayn): A book on Hanafi transactions combining two earlier works: Fusul al-'Imadi and Fusul al-Isturushni.
ابن قاضي سماوة (Ibn Qadi Samawa): Title of the Hanafi scholar Badr al-Din Mahmud, author of Jami' al-Fuslayn.
فصول العمادي (Fusul al-'Imadi): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-'Imadi, one of the two sources combined in Jami' al-Fuslayn.
فصول الإستروشني (Fusul al-Isturushni): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Isturushni, the other source combined in Jami' al-Fuslayn.
المعاملات (al-mu'amalat): Transactions, contracts, and financial dealings; the subject of Jami' al-Fuslayn.

Al-Jami' al-Kabir: The Great Compilation of Hanafi Fiqh
Introduction to al-Jami' al-Kabir and its variants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Jami' al-Kabir by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, state its significance, and list later Hanafi scholars who authored works with the same title.

Core Idea
Al-Jami' al-Kabir by Muhammad al-Shaybani is the foundational Hanafi fiqh compilation; later scholars produced their own 'Jami's' as commentaries or independent works.

The passage introduces al-Jami' al-Kabir, the magnum opus of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, and then lists other Hanafi scholars who authored works by the same name. Understanding which 'Jami' is being referenced is crucial for navigating Hanafi sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and work
Recognize that al-Jami' al-Kabir is attributed to Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, a direct student of Imam Abu Hanifa.
Al-Shaybani's Jami' is considered the most authoritative.
2
Understand the praise by Shaykh Akmal al-Din
Read the quoted praise: the work encompasses the 'finest narrations and texts of knowledge' and is described as nearly miraculous.
This indicates the high esteem for the work.
3
Note the historical reward for memorization
King al-Mu'azzam 'Isa gave 100 dinars for memorizing al-Jami' al-Kabir and 50 for al-Jami' al-Saghir.
This reflects the immense value placed on memorizing these texts.
4
List the multiple ‘Jami' al-Kabir’ works
The passage enumerates other Hanafi scholars who authored works titled al-Jami' al-Kabir: al-Bazdawi, al-Isbijabi, al-Samarqandi, al-Sadr al-Hamid, Qadikhan, and al-'Attabi.
These are distinct from al-Shaybani's work but share the same name.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكتب الواردة في الشرح العلم في صباه عن والده وحفظ القرآن وقرأ بقونية من بلاد الروم بعضاً من العلوم وعلم النجوم على مولانا فيض الله من تلامذة مولانا فضل ومكث أربعة أشهر. ولما توفى مولانا فيض الله ارتحل إلى الديار المصرية، وقرأ هنالك مع السيد الشريف الجرجاني على مبارك شاه المنطقى المدرس بالقاهرة، وقرأ مع السيد على أكمل الدين البابرتي، وبرع في جميع العلوم. وله تصانيف كثيرة منها: لطائف الإشارات في الفقه وجامع الفصولين وعنقود الجواهر شرح كتاب المقصود في الصرف، وكانت وفاته سنة ٨١٨ تقريبا. ومن شركاءه في درسه المولى العالم الحاج باشاه، صاحب كتاب الشفاء والتسهيل في الطب، وحواشي شرح المطالع وشرح الطوالع. وكان السيد الشريف يشهد لهما بالفضيلة كذا في الشقائق النعمانية. وهو مخالف لما ذكره صاحب الكشف في اسم أبيه وسنة وفاته فافهم.
٢٤ الجامع الكبير: للإمام محمد بن الحسن الشيباني، صاحب الإمام أبي حنيفة رحمه الله. قال الشيخ أكمل الدين: "هو كاسمه الجلائل مسائل الفقه، جامع كبير قد اشتمل على عيون الروايات ومتون الدرايات بحيث كاد أن يكون معجزا، ولتمام لطائف الفقه منجزاً، شهد بذلك بعد إنفاد العمر فيه راووه. ولا يكاد يلم بشيء من ذلك عادوه، ولذلك امتدت أعناق ذوى التحقيق نحو تحقيقه، واشتدت رغباتهم في الاعتناء بحلى لفظه وتطبيقه، وكتبوا له شروحا، وجعلوه مبيناً ومشروحاً". انتهى. وكان من عادة الملك المعظم عيسى بن أبي بكر الأيوبي صاحب الشام المتوفى سنة ٦٢٤ هـ أن يعطي مائة دينار لمن يحفظ الجامع الكبير، وخمسين ديناراً لمن يحفظ الجامع الصغير.
ثم اعلم أن "الجامع الكبير" لأصحابنا متعدد، وقد عدده صاحب "الحقائق" .. وقال: منها: الجامع الكبير لفخر الإسلام على البزدوي، وللإمام قطب الدين أبي الحسن علي بن محمد الإسبيجابي، ولشيخ الإسلام علاء الدين السمرقندي، وللصدر الحميد، ولفخر الدين قاضيخان وللعتابي. والظاهر أن لهم مصنفات بذلك الاسم كما لأبي الحسن الكرخي غير الشروح المذكورة في جامع محمد بن الحسن.
٢٥ الجرجانيات: هي مسائل جمعها محمد رحمه الله بجرجان كما في حاشية الطحطاوي على المراقى (ص ١٠). وفي الكشف (١/٥٨١) هي مسائل رواها علي بن صالح الجرجاني عن محمد بن الحسن رحمه الله.
٢٦ الجوهرة النيرة: راجع "السراج الوهاج".
٢٧ حاشية الأشباه للرملي: هي "نزهة النواظر على الأشباه والنظائر"، حاشية مختصرة للعلامة خير الدين الرملي صاحب الفتاوى الخيرية، وهي مطبوعة. حاشية الحموي غمز عيون البصائر في آخر الجلد الرابع. راجع الفتاوى الخيرية مع الصواب [؟] تر المحمول إلى نعرہ انکے حقول [؟]
٢٨ حاشية البزدوي: وهي حاشية على كنز الأصول الشهير بأصول البزدوي وكلاهما لفخر الإسلام أبي العسر علي بن محمد بن الحسن بن عبد الكريم ابن موسى بن عيسى بن مجاهد البزدوي، فقيه أصولي، محدث، ولد سنة ٤٠٠ هـ، وتوفى سنة ٤٨٢ هـ، من تصانيفه "شرح الجامع الكبير للشيباني". انظر: تاريخ بغداد (١٢/٧٠، ٧١) ومعجم المؤلفين (٢/٥٠١).
٢٩ حاشية الحلبي على الدر المختار: للعلامة إبراهيم بن محمد ابن إبراهيم الحلبي، مؤلف شرحي منية المصلي الصغير والكبير. كان إمامًا وخطيبًا بجامع السلطان محمد خان بالقسطنطينية. ومات في ٩٥٦ هـ وقد جاوز التسعين. وللزيادة راجع "الشيخ إبراهيم الحلبي" في الأعلام.
The books mentioned in the commentary: He sought knowledge in his youth from his father, memorized the Quran, and studied in Konya from the lands of Rum some of the sciences and the science of astronomy under our master Fayd Allah from the students of our master Fadl, and stayed for four months. When our master Fayd Allah died, he traveled to the Egyptian lands, and read there with al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani under Mubarak Shah al-Mantiqi the teacher in Cairo, and read with al-Sayyid Ali Akmal al-Din al-Babarti, and excelled in all sciences. He has many works, including: Lata'if al-Isharat in fiqh, Jami' al-Fusulayn, and Unqud al-Jawahir commentary on al-Maqsud in morphology. His death was around the year 818. Among his companions in study was the scholar al-Hajj Bashah, author of al-Shifa' wa al-Tashil in medicine, and glosses on Sharh al-Matali' and Sharh al-Tawali'. Al-Sayyid al-Sharif testified to their excellence, as in al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya. It contradicts what the author of al-Kashf mentioned regarding his father's name and the year of his death, so understand.
24. Al-Jami' al-Kabir: by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, the companion of Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him). Shaykh Akmal al-Din said: "It is, as its name suggests, the majesties of fiqh issues, a great collection that encompasses the finest narrations and texts of knowledge to the extent that it is almost miraculous, and for the completion of fiqh subtleties it is effective, as its narrators testified after spending their lives upon it. And hardly any of their opponents can grasp anything of it, and therefore the necks of the people of verification extended towards its verification, and their desires intensified in caring for the adornment of its wording and its application, and they wrote commentaries on it, and made it clearly explained and commented upon." End. And it was the custom of King al-Mu'azzam 'Isa ibn Abi Bakr al-Ayyubi, the ruler of al-Sham who died in 624 AH, to give a hundred dinars to whoever memorized al-Jami' al-Kabir, and fifty dinars to whoever memorized al-Jami' al-Saghir.
Then know that "al-Jami' al-Kabir" for our companions is multiple, and the author of al-Haqa'iq has enumerated them... He said: Among them: al-Jami' al-Kabir of Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi, and of Imam Qutb al-Din Abi al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Isbijabi, and of Shaykh al-Islam 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi, and of al-Sadr al-Hamid, and of Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan, and of al-'Attabi. And it appears that they have works by that name just as Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi has works besides the commentaries mentioned in Jami' Muhammad ibn al-Hasan.
25. al-Jurjaniyyat: They are issues that Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) collected in Jurjan, as in al-Tahtawi's gloss on al-Muraqi (p. 10). And in al-Kashf (1/581) they are issues narrated by Ali ibn Salih al-Jurjani from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (may Allah have mercy on him).
26. al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah: See al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
27. Hashiyat al-Ashbah li al-Ramli: It is Nuzhat al-Nawazir 'ala al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, a concise gloss by al-'Allamah Khayr al-Din al-Ramli, author of al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah, and it is printed. Hashiyat al-Hamawi 'Ghamz 'Uyun al-Basa'ir' at the end of the fourth volume. See al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah with the correction. [؟] Transfer the carried to our field fields [؟].
28. Hashiyat al-Bazdawi: It is a gloss on Kanz al-Usul famous as Usul al-Bazdawi, both by Fakhr al-Islam Abi al-'Usr Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Abd al-Karim ibn Musa ibn 'Isa ibn Mujahid al-Bazdawi, a jurisprudential theologian, hadith scholar, born in 400 AH, and died in 482 AH. Among his works is Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir lil-Shaybani. See: Tarikh Baghdad (12/70, 71) and Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (2/501).
29. Hashiyat al-Halabi 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar: by al-'Allamah Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Halabi, author of the two commentaries on Munyat al-Musalli: the small and the large. He was an imam and khatib at the Mosque of Sultan Muhammad Khan in Constantinople. He died in 956 AH, having exceeded ninety. For more, see "Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi" in al-A'lam.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter section of a commentary, listing important Hanafi reference works and providing brief biographical notes on their authors. It begins with an unnumbered biographical entry (likely the author of the commentary or a previous scholar), detailing his studies, teachers, and works. Then it enumerates specific books: entry 24 describes al-Jami' al-Kabir by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, extolled by Shaykh Akmal al-Din, and notes the historical reward for memorizing it. It also mentions other works titled al-Jami' al-Kabir by later Hanafi scholars. Entry 25 defines al-Jurjaniyyat as issues collected by Muhammad al-Shaybani in Jurjan. Entry 26 refers to al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah via al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Entry 27 covers al-Ramli's gloss on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. Entry 28 gives a biography of al-Bazdawi and his gloss on his own Usul. Entry 29 discusses al-Halabi's gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The passage serves as a valuable reference for students of Hanafi fiqh and usul, identifying key texts and their positions within the school.

Key Terms
الجامع الكبير (al-Jami' al-Kabir): A major collection of Hanafi fiqh rulings by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani; also the name of similar works by later Hanafi scholars.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the reward given by King al-Mu'azzam 'Isa for memorizing al-Jami' al-Kabir?
A) Fifty dinars
B) One hundred dinars
C) One thousand dinars
D) A robe of honor

Key Takeaway
Al-Jami' al-Kabir is a foundational Hanafi text by al-Shaybani, but later scholars also authored works with the same title—context is key.

Life of the Author

Key Reference Works: Al-Jurjaniyyat, Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, and Three Major Glosses
Brief entries on four reference works and three glosses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the textual nature and authorship of al-Jurjaniyyat, al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, and the three glosses (al-Ramli, al-Bazdawi, al-Halabi) mentioned in the passage.

Core Idea
Al-Jurjaniyyat is a rare transmission from al-Shaybani; the three glosses are essential later commentaries on core Hanafi works.

This lesson covers the remaining reference entries from the passage: al-Jurjaniyyat (a collection of issues by al-Shaybani transmitted via al-Jurjani), al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah (a later commentary), and three important glosses on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, Usul al-Bazdawi, and al-Durr al-Mukhtar. Understanding these works is vital for advanced study and fatwa research.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Jurjaniyyat's transmission
Recognize that al-Jurjaniyyat are issues collected by Muhammad al-Shaybani in Jurjan, narrated by Ali ibn Salih al-Jurjani. This is part of the nawadir (rare transmissions).
Reference to al-Tahtawi's gloss and al-Kashf confirms the transmission.
2
Locate al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah
Note the cross-reference to 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj', indicating that al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah is a commentary to be sought under that name.
This shows how later works are interconnected.
3
Identify the three glosses
List the three glosses: Hashiyat al-Ashbah (al-Ramli), Hashiyat al-Bazdawi (by al-Bazdawi himself on his own Usul), and Hashiyat al-Halabi on al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Each gloss has a distinct purpose and base text.
4
Note the biographical details
For each gloss, note the author's death dates and key works: al-Ramli (author of al-Fatawa al-Khayriyah), al-Bazdawi (born 400, died 482), and al-Halabi (died 956).
These dates help place the works in the Hanafi tradition.

الكتب الواردة في الشرح العلم في صباه عن والده وحفظ القرآن وقرأ بقونية من بلاد الروم بعضاً من العلوم وعلم النجوم على مولانا فيض الله من تلامذة مولانا فضل ومكث أربعة أشهر. ولما توفى مولانا فيض الله ارتحل إلى الديار المصرية، وقرأ هنالك مع السيد الشريف الجرجاني على مبارك شاه المنطقى المدرس بالقاهرة، وقرأ مع السيد على أكمل الدين البابرتي، وبرع في جميع العلوم. وله تصانيف كثيرة منها: لطائف الإشارات في الفقه وجامع الفصولين وعنقود الجواهر شرح كتاب المقصود في الصرف، وكانت وفاته سنة ٨١٨ تقريبا. ومن شركاءه في درسه المولى العالم الحاج باشاه، صاحب كتاب الشفاء والتسهيل في الطب، وحواشي شرح المطالع وشرح الطوالع. وكان السيد الشريف يشهد لهما بالفضيلة كذا في الشقائق النعمانية. وهو مخالف لما ذكره صاحب الكشف في اسم أبيه وسنة وفاته فافهم.

The books mentioned in the commentary: He sought knowledge in his youth from his father, memorized the Quran, and studied in Konya from the lands of Rum some of the sciences and the science of astronomy under our master Fayd Allah from the students of our master Fadl, and stayed for four months. When our master Fayd Allah died, he traveled to the Egyptian lands, and read there with al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani under Mubarak Shah al-Mantiqi the teacher in Cairo, and read with al-Sayyid Ali Akmal al-Din al-Babarti, and excelled in all sciences. He has many works, including: Lata'if al-Isharat in fiqh, Jami' al-Fusulayn, and Unqud al-Jawahir commentary on al-Maqsud in morphology. His death was around the year 818. Among his companions in study was the scholar al-Hajj Bashah, author of al-Shifa' wa al-Tashil in medicine, and glosses on Sharh al-Matali' and Sharh al-Tawali'. Al-Sayyid al-Sharif testified to their excellence, as in al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya. It contradicts what the author of al-Kashf mentioned regarding his father's name and the year of his death, so understand.
24. Al-Jami' al-Kabir: by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, the companion of Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him). Shaykh Akmal al-Din said: "It is, as its name suggests, the majesties of fiqh issues, a great collection that encompasses the finest narrations and texts of knowledge to the extent that it is almost miraculous, and for the completion of fiqh subtleties it is effective, as its narrators testified after spending their lives upon it. And hardly any of their opponents can grasp anything of it, and therefore the necks of the people of verification extended towards its verification, and their desires intensified in caring for the adornment of its wording and its application, and they wrote commentaries on it, and made it clearly explained and commented upon." End. And it was the custom of King al-Mu'azzam 'Isa ibn Abi Bakr al-Ayyubi, the ruler of al-Sham who died in 624 AH, to give a hundred dinars to whoever memorized al-Jami' al-Kabir, and fifty dinars to whoever memorized al-Jami' al-Saghir.
Then know that "al-Jami' al-Kabir" for our companions is multiple, and the author of al-Haqa'iq has enumerated them... He said: Among them: al-Jami' al-Kabir of Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi, and of Imam Qutb al-Din Abi al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Isbijabi, and of Shaykh al-Islam 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi, and of al-Sadr al-Hamid, and of Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan, and of al-'Attabi. And it appears that they have works by that name just as Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi has works besides the commentaries mentioned in Jami' Muhammad ibn al-Hasan.
25. al-Jurjaniyyat: They are issues that Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) collected in Jurjan, as in al-Tahtawi's gloss on al-Muraqi (p. 10). And in al-Kashf (1/581) they are issues narrated by Ali ibn Salih al-Jurjani from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (may Allah have mercy on him).
26. al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah: See al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
27. Hashiyat al-Ashbah li al-Ramli: It is Nuzhat al-Nawazir 'ala al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, a concise gloss by al-'Allamah Khayr al-Din al-Ramli, author of al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah, and it is printed. Hashiyat al-Hamawi 'Ghamz 'Uyun al-Basa'ir' at the end of the fourth volume. See al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah with the correction. [؟] Transfer the carried to our field fields [؟].
28. Hashiyat al-Bazdawi: It is a gloss on Kanz al-Usul famous as Usul al-Bazdawi, both by Fakhr al-Islam Abi al-'Usr Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn 'Abd al-Karim ibn Musa ibn 'Isa ibn Mujahid al-Bazdawi, a jurisprudential theologian, hadith scholar, born in 400 AH, and died in 482 AH. Among his works is Sharh al-Jami' al-Kabir lil-Shaybani. See: Tarikh Baghdad (12/70, 71) and Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (2/501).
29. Hashiyat al-Halabi 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar: by al-'Allamah Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Halabi, author of the two commentaries on Munyat al-Musalli: the small and the large. He was an imam and khatib at the Mosque of Sultan Muhammad Khan in Constantinople. He died in 956 AH, having exceeded ninety. For more, see "Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi" in al-A'lam.

Then it enumerates specific books: entry 24 describes al-Jami' al-Kabir by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, extolled by Shaykh Akmal al-Din, and notes the historical reward for memorizing it. It also mentions other works titled al-Jami' al-Kabir by later Hanafi scholars. Entry 25 defines al-Jurjaniyyat as issues collected by Muhammad al-Shaybani in Jurjan. Entry 26 refers to al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah via al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Entry 27 covers al-Ramli's gloss on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. Entry 28 gives a biography of al-Bazdawi and his gloss on his own Usul. Entry 29 discusses al-Halabi's gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. The passage serves as a valuable reference for students of Hanafi fiqh and usul, identifying key texts and their positions within the school.

Key Terms
الجرجانيات (al-Jurjaniyyat): A collection of fiqh issues narrated by Ali ibn Salih al-Jurjani from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Ibrahim al-Halabi

Key Takeaway
Al-Jurjaniyyat is a rare transmission from al-Shaybani, and the three glosses are critical tools for accessing Hanafi usul and fiqh.

Al-Haqa'iq: A Hanafi Commentary by a Polymath Scholar
Biographical and bibliographic notice on 'al-Haqa'iq'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, his scholarly qualifications, and the significance of his commentary 'al-Haqa'iq' within the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Haqa'iq is a seven-year commentary merging fiqh, hadith, tafsir, and usul by a Bukharan scholar martyred in 671 AH.

This lesson introduces the work 'al-Haqa'iq', a commentary on al-Nasafi's versified legal text. Knowing the author's background—a jurist, hadith scholar, exegete, theologian, and man of letters—helps us appreciate the depth and authority of this commentary. The passage also provides key bibliographic data: the work took over seven years to complete and its manuscript resides in Medina.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and its subject
Al-Haqa'iq is a commentary (sharh) on al-Manzumah by al-Nasafi. Note that it is a sharh on a versified legal text.
Versified texts (manzumah) were common for memorization.
2
Analyze the author's credentials
The author, Abu al-Mahamid al-Isfanji, is described as a faqih, muhaddith, hafiz, mufassir, usuli, mutakallim, adib. This breadth indicates the commentary integrates multiple disciplines.
This list of titles shows his mastery of both transmitted and rational sciences.
3
Extract biographical milestones
Note his birth in 627 AH and martyrdom in 671 AH. The commentary was completed in 666 AH.
The completion date (Eid al-Adha) shows dedication over seven years.
4
Assess scholarly significance
The passage states the commentary is 'unique in style' and 'circulated among scholars'. This suggests it is a respected text in the Hanafi tradition.
5
Trace manuscript location
The manuscript is in Medina, indicating its preservation and accessibility.
Medina is a major center for manuscript collections.

Identifying an Early Hanafi Work (261 AH)
Bibliographic description of an early Hanafi manuscript

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract and evaluate key bibliographic details of a 3rd-century Hanafi work from a descriptive entry.

Core Idea
A single work may appear in different volumes and editions, so careful bibliographic verification is essential.

This lesson examines a brief entry from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti that describes a work by an early Hanafi scholar who died in 261 AH. The text notes contradictory reports about the number of volumes and provides the author's own observation of a printed edition. Such entries help the mufti trace the transmission and authenticity of source texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the entry
The entry refers to 'al-kutub al-waridah fi al-sharh' (the books mentioned in the commentary) by a scholar who died in 261 AH. Note that the scholar's name is not explicitly given here, but later works identify him.
The death date (261 AH) places him in the early third century, making this a very early Hanafi work.
2
Extract the bibliographic claims
The author of al-Kashf states the work is in two volumes; al-Tamimi mentions it in his Tabaqat. The commentator says he saw a single small volume printed in Cairo in 1314 AH with 56 chapters.
This variation in volume count may indicate different recensions or abridgments.
3
Analyse the chain of transmission in the opening
The work begins with a chain: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Umar ibn Muhayr al-Shaybani, who narrates from Salamah ibn Salih. This suggests the work is a collection of hadith or legal narrations.
The name 'Muhayr' may be a scribal error; correct form is unclear.
4
Evaluate the significance for Hanafi scholarship
Identifying such works helps establish the early textual basis for Hanafi rulings. The fact that a printed copy existed in 1314 AH indicates its ongoing use.
The 56 chapters likely cover major fiqh topics; the chain suggests reliance on early authorities.

الكتب الواردة في الشرح المتوفى (٢٦١هـ)، قال صاحب الكشف: هو في مجلدين. ذكره التميمي في طبقات الحنفية. انتهى. أقول: وأنا رأيته في مجلد واحد صغير الحجم طبع بمصر القاهرة في سنة ١٣١٤هـ. وكان مشتملا على ست وخمسين من الأبواب، كما عددتها. وأوله: رب يسر، قال أبو بكر أحمد بن عمر بن مهير الشيباني. حدثنا سلمة بن صالح... إلخ.

Its beginning is: 'O Lord, make easy,' said Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Umar ibn Muhayr al-Shaybani. Salamah ibn Salih narrated to us... etc.

Al-Khaniyyah: The Relied-Upon Fatwa Collection of Qadikhan
Description of a well-known fatwa collection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the significance of al-Khaniyyah in Hanafi fatwa practice and identify the author's methodology in selecting opinions.

Core Idea
Al-Khaniyyah is a practical fatwa collection focused on common incidents, not comprehensive fiqh.

In this passage, we learn about one of the most important fatwa collections in the Hanafi school: al-Fatawa al-Khaniyyah by Qadikhan. This work is not a theoretical fiqh manual like al-Hidayah, but a compilation of actual fatwas on issues that repeatedly occur. Understanding its role helps a mufti know where to look for authoritative answers to real-world problems.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his scholarly background
Note the full name and lineage: Imam Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan Hasan ibn Mansur al-Uzjandi al-Farghani. This establishes his authority.
2
Assess the reputation and usage of the work
The text says it is 'famous, accepted, acted upon, and circulated among scholars and jurists'. It is printed on the margin of al-Alamgiriyyah, indicating its complementary status.
3
Understand the selection methodology
Qadikhan confined himself to one or two opinions from later scholars, presenting the most apparent (azhar) view. This demonstrates a tarjih approach for practical fatwa.
4
Note the arrangement and later reorganization
The work follows standard fiqh chapter order. A scholar from Rum later rearranged issues and named it Wahaj al-Shari'ah. Knowing this helps locate relevant fatwas.
5
Recognize the author's other works
The passage lists four unpublished works, showing Qadikhan's breadth in commentary and legal theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخانية فتاوى قاضيخان: هي للإمام فخر الدين قاضيخان حسن بن منصور الأوزجندي الفرغاني. وهذه الفتاوى مشهورة مقبولة، معمول بها، متداولة بين أيدي العلماء والفقهاء، مطبوعة على هامش العالمكيرية، وهي نصب عين من تصدر للحكم والإفتاء، وذكر في هذا الكتاب جملة من المسائل التي يغلب وقوعها، وتمس الحاجة إليها، وتدور عليها واقعات الأمة. وترتيبه على ترتيب الكتب المعروفة بين العلماء فرعًا وأصلا. وما كثرت فيه الأقاويل من المتأخرين اقتصر منه على قول أو قولين، وقدم ما هو الأظهر كما قال في خطبته. وقد رتب رجل من أهل الروم مسائله وأول المرتب "الحمد لله الذي هدانا لهذا وما كنا لنهتدي لولا أن هدانا الله... إلخ" ذكر فيه أنه أشار إليه شيخه المولى محمد ابن شيخ الإسلام محمد الشهير بـ "جوی زاده سنة ٥٩٥ هـ بترتيبه فرتبه وسماه وهاج الشريعة واسمه "تاريخ الترتيب" كذا في الكشف. وأما كتبه الأخرى غير المطبوعة، فهي: ١- الأمالی، ۲- شرح الزيادات، ۳- شرح الجامع الصغير، ٤- شرح أدب القاضي للخصاف. وأوزجند اسم موضع قريب من فرغانة.
Al-Khaniyyah: Fatwas of Qadikhan: It is by Imam Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan Hasan ibn Mansur al-Uzjandi al-Farghani. These fatwas are famous, accepted, acted upon, and circulated among scholars and jurists, printed on the margin of al-Alamgiriyyah, and they are the focus of those who take up judgment and issuing fatwas. He mentioned in this book a number of issues that commonly occur, are needed, and around which the incidents of the Ummah revolve. Its arrangement follows the arrangement of books known among scholars, both furu' and usul. Wherever there were many sayings among the later scholars, he confined himself to one or two sayings, and presented the most apparent as he said in his preface. A man from Rum arranged its issues, and the beginning of the arranged work is 'Praise be to Allah who guided us to this, and we would not have been guided had Allah not guided us... etc.' He mentioned that his teacher, Mawlana Muhammad ibn Shaykh al-Islam Muhammad, famous as 'Juy Zadeh' in 595 AH, indicated to him to arrange it, so he arranged it and named it 'Wahaj al-Shari'ah' and its name is 'Tarikh al-Tartib'. Thus in al-Kashf. As for his other unpublished works, they are: 1. al-Amali, 2. Sharh al-Ziyadat, 3. Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, 4. Sharh Adab al-Qadi lil-Khassaf. And Uzjand is a place name near Farghana.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage describes the famous Hanafi fatwa collection 'al-Fatawa al-Khaniyyah' by Qadikhan (d. 592 AH). It explains that the work is well-known, reliable, and widely used, often printed alongside the Fatawa al-Alamgiriyyah. The collection focuses on commonly occurring issues and is arranged in the standard fiqh chapter order. The author (Qadikhan) often selects only one or two opinions from later scholars, preferring the most apparent view. Later, a scholar from Rum (Anatolia) rearranged the issues and named it 'Wahaj al-Shari'ah' or 'Tarikh al-Tartib'. The passage also lists Qadikhan's other unpublished works, highlighting his scholarly output. This entry is crucial for understanding the sources of Hanafi fatwa practice and the hierarchy of works used in ifta'.

Key Terms
الخانية (al-Khaniyyah): Short for 'al-Fatawa al-Khaniyyah', the fatwa collection of Qadikhan.
قاضيخان (Qadikhan): Title of Fakhr al-Din Hasan ibn Mansur al-Uzjandi, a leading Hanafi jurist and author of the Khaniyyah fatwas.
الأظهر (al-azhar): The most apparent or preponderant opinion among multiple views.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He included all possible opinions from early and later scholars.
B) He limited the discussion to one or two opinions and presented the most apparent.
C) He only included his own fatwas.
D) He arranged the book alphabetically.

Key Takeaway
Al-Khaniyyah is a highly respected fatwa collection that selects the most apparent opinion for common issues, making it an indispensable reference for Hanafi muftis.

Al-Khaniyya (Fatawa Qadikhan): A Cornerstone of Hanafi Fatwa
Introduces a major Hanafi fatwa collection and its author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the significance of Fatawa Qadikhan within the Hanafi fatwa tradition and identify its key features.

Core Idea
Fatawa Qadikhan provides authoritative, widely accepted rulings on frequently occurring issues, arranged in the standard Hanafi chapter order.

In the Hanafi tradition, certain fatwa collections achieve such widespread acceptance that they become essential references for muftis. One such work is Al-Khaniyya, better known as Fatawa Qadikhan. This lesson introduces the author, the unique features of his compilation, and its place in the hierarchy of Hanafi fatwa sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his background
The passage names the author as Imam Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan Hasan ibn Mansur al-Uzjandi al-Farghani. Note his full name and regional affiliation.
He lived in the 6th century AH (12th century CE) and was a prominent Hanafi jurist from Transoxiana.
2
Assess the status of the book
The text describes the book as 'famous, accepted, acted upon, circulated among scholars and jurists, printed on the margin of al-Alamgiriyya'. This indicates high authority and widespread use.
Al-Alamgiriyya (Fatawa Alamgiriyya) is a later authoritative compilation; being printed on its margin shows the work's importance.
3
Understand the compilation method
Qadikhan focused on issues that 'frequently occur, are needed, and around which the events of the community revolve'. He limited conflicting opinions to one or two statements and presented the more apparent view.
This makes the work practical and accessible for muftis dealing with common cases.
4
Note the arrangement
The book follows the standard order of Hanafi fiqh chapters, both branches (furu') and principles (usul), making it easy to navigate.
This arrangement mirrors major Hanafi reference works.
5
Identify later developments
A scholar from Anatolia (Rum) rearranged the work under the title 'Wahaj al-Shari'ah' (or 'Tarikh al-Tartib'), as mentioned in Kashf al-Zunun.
This reflects the ongoing engagement with the text by later scholars.

Khizanat al-Akmal: A Comprehensive Fiqh Encyclopedia
Describing a Hanafi fiqh encyclopedia and a biographical discrepancy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the chronological and geographical origins of Khizanat al-Akmal and evaluate conflicting biographical claims about its author using textual criticism.

Core Idea
Khizanat al-Akmal is a six-volume Hanafi fiqh encyclopedia; its author's identity is disputed, teaching us to verify biographical chains.

This lesson introduces an important later Hanafi reference work, Khizanat al-Akmal. We will examine its structure, the works it encompasses, and a scholarly dispute about its author's teachers. Understanding such biographical details helps a mufti assess the authority of the opinions cited in the work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and its scope
Note the title, number of volumes, and field (furu' al-fiqh). The passage states it is in six volumes on substantive Hanafi law.
2
List the earlier works it covers
The author claims his book encompasses the solutions from many earlier texts. Identify the key ones: Kafi al-Hakim, al-Jami'ayn, al-Ziyadat, etc.
This shows Khizanat al-Akmal is a later compilation, not a primary source.
3
Examine the author's identity
The passage gives two versions of the author's name: Yusuf ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jurjani and Yusuf ibn Muhammad al-Jurjani. Also note the disagreement about his death date and teacher.
The name difference might indicate confusion between two individuals.
4
Analyze the chronological dispute
Al-Kashf says the author (or a commentator with the same name?) died in 398 AH, while al-Karkhi died in 340 AH. If correct, al-Jurjani could not have studied under al-Karkhi. This is a classic case of verifying isnad through dates.
This teaches the importance of chronology in biographical criticism.
5
Assess the lesson for a mufti
A mufti using Khizanat al-Akmal must recognize it as a 6th-century compilation, not a primary source. Its authority comes from gathering earlier views; knowing its date and disputed authorship affects how one weighs its rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۸- خزانة الأكمل : هو في الفروع ست مجلدات، لأبي يعقوب، يوسف ابن علی بن محمد الجرجاني الحنفي. ذكر فيه أن هذا الكتاب محيط يحل مصنفات الأصحاب . بدأ بكافي الحاكم ، ثم بالجامعين ثم بالزيادات ثم بمجرد بن زياد (وهو حسن ابن زياد اللؤلؤى والمنتقى والكرخي وشرح الطحاوى وعيون المسائل وغير ذلك ، واتفق ابتداءه يوم عيد الأضحى سنة اثنتين وعشرين وخمسمائة كذا في الكشف . وفيه نص على أن مصنفه يوسف بن على بن محمد الجرجاني، وهو المستفاد من الجواهر المضيئة حيث ذكر فيه : "يوسف بن علی بن محمد الجرجاني أبو عبد الله ، تفقه على أبي الحسن الكرخي كان عالما، تفقه على أبي حنيفة وأصحابه ومن تصانيفه خزانة الأكمل فی ست مجلدات " . وأورده صاحب الفوائد في ترجمة يوسف بن محمد ، وقال : يوسف بن محمد أبو عبد الله الجرجاني كان عالما يرحل إليه في الواقعات وله خزانة الأكمل وغيره. لكن القارى ذكر نسبه يوسف بن علی بن محمد والذي في الكشف : هو أن شارح الجامع الكبير هو أبو عبد الله الجرجاني المتوفى سنة ٣٩٨هـ وقال عند ذكر " خزانة الأكمل " إلى آخره : وهذا إن كان صحيحاً لم يكن ما ذكره الكفوى من تلمذه على الكرخي صحيحا : إذ وفاة الكرخي على ما مر ٣٤٠هـ انتهى ما في الفوائد مختصراً.
38- Khizanat al-Akmal: It is on furu' (substantive law), six volumes, by Abu Ya'qub, Yusuf ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jurjani al-Hanafi. He mentioned in it that this book encompasses the solutions to the writings of the companions (of Abu Hanifa). He began with Kafi al-Hakim, then al-Jami'ayn, then al-Ziyadat, then Mujarrad ibn Ziyad (and it is Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i), and al-Muntaqa, and al-Karkhi, and Sharh al-Tahawi, and 'Uyun al-Masa'il, and others. Its commencement occurred on the day of Eid al-Adha in the year 522 AH, as mentioned in al-Kashf. In it there is a statement that its author is Yusuf ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jurjani, which is derived from al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a where it mentions: 'Yusuf ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jurjani, Abu Abd Allah, studied under Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, was a scholar, studied under Abu Hanifa and his companions, and among his works is Khizanat al-Akmal in six volumes.' And the author of al-Fawa'id mentioned him in the biography of Yusuf ibn Muhammad, saying: 'Yusuf ibn Muhammad Abu Abd Allah al-Jurjani was a scholar who was traveled to for events, and he has Khizanat al-Akmal and others.' But al-Qari mentioned his lineage as Yusuf ibn Ali ibn Muhammad, and what is in al-Kashf is that the commentator of al-Jami' al-Kabir is Abu Abd Allah al-Jurjani who died in 398 AH, and he said when mentioning Khizanat al-Akmal: 'If this is correct, then what al-Kafawi mentioned about his studying under al-Karkhi is not correct, since the death of al-Karkhi, as per what passed, is 340 AH.' End of what is in al-Fawa'id, summarized.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage introduces Khizanat al-Akmal, a six-volume work on Hanafi furu' by Abu Ya'qub Yusuf al-Jurjani. The author claims his book encompasses the solutions to all earlier Hanafi texts, listing major works it covers. The passage also contains a scholarly disagreement: al-Qari and al-Kashf identify the author as Yusuf ibn Ali who died in 398 AH, which would make it impossible for him to have studied under al-Karkhi (d. 340 AH) as some claimed. This highlights the importance of verifying isnad and biographical data.

Key Terms
خزانة الأكمل (Khizanat al-Akmal): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh work in six volumes, covering many earlier texts.
أبو يعقوب يوسف الجرجاني (Abu Ya'qub Yusuf al-Jurjani): The author of Khizanat al-Akmal, a Hanafi jurist, possibly of the 4th-5th century AH.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when did the composition of Khizanat al-Akmal begin?
A) 340 AH
B) 398 AH
C) 522 AH
D) 1128 CE

Key Takeaway
Biographical and chronological criticism is essential when using later Hanafi compilations; always verify the author's death date and chain of transmission to assess the weight of the work.

Khizanat al-Riwayat: A Collection with Rare Narrations and Caution on Authority
A biographical entry about a fiqh collection and its authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and content of Khizanat al-Riwayat and explain why some Hanafi scholars do not rely on it.

Core Idea
Not every compilation of rare narrations carries full authority – Khizanat al-Riwayat is one such collection treated with caution.

This passage introduces Khizanat al-Riwayat, a work on furu' al-fiqh by al-Qadi Jakan al-Hanafi al-Hindi. It collects issues and rare narrations, but as Shaykh al-Anwar notes, it is not fully relied upon. Understanding this distinction is essential for a mufti in evaluating sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and its subject
The work is Khizanat al-Riwayat, which focuses on furu' al-fiqh (positive law). Note that it is a compilation of rulings and rare narrations.
Furu' means the branches of fiqh, as opposed to usul.
2
Note the author and his origin
The author is al-Qadi Jakan al-Hanafi al-Hindi, a Hanafi judge from Gujarat, India. Recognize that he is a later scholar from the Indian subcontinent.
The text spells 'Jakan' and gives his locale as 'Kan' in Gujarat.
3
Recognize the content: collection of issues and rare narrations
The author states he spent his life collecting masail and gharib al-riwayat (rare narrations). The work begins with Kitab al-'Ilm because knowledge is the noblest act.
Gharib al-riwayat refers to non-mashhur or uncommon narrations.
4
Understand the critical view: Shaykh al-Anwar does not rely on it
Shaykh al-Anwar in Fayd al-Bari explicitly says he does not rely on this book. This indicates a limitation in its authority for fatwa.
This is a crucial caution: not all compiled works are equally authoritative.
5
Note the reasoning for beginning with Kitab al-'Ilm
The author began with the book of knowledge because he considered it the most noble form of worship. This reflects his prioritization.
It does not affect the fiqh authority but shows author's piety.

Source Text

(۱۲۳-۳) وقال في الكشف : خزانة الروايات فى الفروع للقاضي جكن الحنفى الهندي الساكن بقصبة "كن من الكجرات، وهو مجلد أوله الحمد لله الذي خلق الإنسان وعلمه البيان" . ذكر فيه : أنه أفنى فيه عمره جمع المسائل وغريب الروايات، وابتدأ بكتاب العلم؛ لأنه أشرف العبادات .

This passage gives two perspectives on Khizanat al-Riwayat. First, a critical view: Shaykh al-Anwar does not rely on it. Second, a descriptive view from al-Kashf, stating it is a one-volume work by al-Qadi Jakan al-Hindi, focusing on issues and rare narrations. The author prioritized the book of knowledge (Kitab al-'Ilm) as it is the most virtuous. This entry illustrates that not all texts are equally authoritative; some are met with caution.

The phrase 'comprehensive of narrations, free of excess' highlights its purpose: to include essential transmitted rulings without superfluous commentary.

By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author of Khizanat al-Akmal and evaluate the scholarly dispute regarding his lineage and teachers.

Core Idea
A mufti must verify author identities and timelines to assess the authority of cited texts.

This lesson examines a biographical note from the introduction to Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. The passage clarifies the identity of Yusuf al-Jurjani, author of the six-volume Hanafi fiqh work Khizanat al-Akmal, and addresses a chronological discrepancy in his scholarly lineage. Understanding such details is crucial for a mufti when evaluating the reliability of a reference work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Determine who the passage is about: the author of Khizanat al-Akmal.
The passage discusses multiple names; focus on the main figure.
2
Extract key biographical details
Note the author's full name, teachers, and works mentioned.
Contrast the two versions of his lineage: Yusuf bin Muhammad vs Yusuf bin Ali bin Muhammad.
3
Analyze the chronological dispute
Examine the death dates: al-Karkhi (340 AH) and al-Jurjani (398 AH). Determine if the claim of being his student is plausible.
The author of al-Fawa'id questions al-Kafawi's claim based on the timeline.
4
Evaluate the source reliability
Consider the sources cited: al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a, al-Kashf, and al-Fawa'id. Which is more authoritative?
The passage seems to prefer the version from al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note on the author of Khizanat al-Akmal, a major Hanafi fiqh work. It presents a scholarly discussion about the identity and lineage of its author. The passage clarifies that the author is Yusuf ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jurjani (also known as Abu Abdullah al-Jurjani), who studied under Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi. There is a discrepancy: al-Kafawi claimed he was a student of al-Karkhi, but since al-Karkhi died in 340 AH and al-Jurjani died in 398 AH, the timeline makes it possible. However, the passage notes that if the author of Khizanat al-Akmal is indeed the same as the commentator of al-Jami' al-Kabir, who died in 398 AH, then the claim that he studied under al-Karkhi is chronologically plausible. The discussion highlights the importance of verifying scholarly lineages and the reliability of biographical details.

By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of Khizanat al-Riwayat as a source for fatwa and identify its author.

Not all Khizanah books are authoritative; Khizanat al-Riwayat is not relied upon for fatwa.

This lesson introduces the work Khizanat al-Riwayat and its compiler. Understanding the reliability of fiqh sources is crucial for a mufti; not every book labeled 'Khizanah' carries the same weight. Shaykh al-Anwar's warning about this book teaches us to be discerning in source selection.

Al-Khulasah: Author, Rank, and Significance
Biographical and bibliographical entry on al-Khulasah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author of al-Khulasah, describe his scholarly rank as a mujtahid fi al-masail, and explain the structural features of his book that aid muftis.

Core Idea
Al-Khulasah is a relied-upon Hanafi compendium by a mujtahid fi al-masail, designed with indices to facilitate fatwa-giving.

This passage introduces us to Imam Tahir al-Bukhari, a senior Hanafi jurist of the 6th century, and his famous work al-Khulasah. Understanding his rank as a mujtahid capable of ijtihad in matters not directly narrated from Abu Hanifa, and the meticulous structure of his book, is essential for recognizing the authority of this text in the Hanafi school. The passage also notes a scholarly debate about the original volume count.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author
Read the full name, patronymic, birth and death years (482–542 AH). Note that he was a student of Qadikhan, a major Hanafi authority.
The author is known as Imam Tahir al-Bukhari, also Iftikhar al-Din.
2
Determine his scholarly rank
From the text, Ibn Kamal Basha classified him as a mujtahid fi al-masail, meaning he could derive rulings for novel cases but could not contradict the school's usul and furu'.
This rank is below absolute mujtahid but above muqallid mufti.
3
Understand the purpose of al-Khulasah
The author wrote it at the request of colleagues to create a concise, comprehensive summary of Khizanat al-Waqi'at and Nisab al-Fiqh. It was intended to assist muftis.
The title 'al-Khulasah' means 'the summary'.
4
Note the structural features
The book includes indexes of chapters and sections at the start of each book, uses colors in commentary to clarify where each mas'ala is discussed, and excludes redundant material.
These features made it user-friendly for fatwa-giving.
5
Recognize the volume dispute
The author intended it as a single volume, but later Indian prints came in four volumes. This does not affect its authority.
The original single-volume format is more convenient.

Source Text

٤٠ - الخلاصة : هو للشيخ الإمام طاهر بن أحمد بن عبد الرشيد بن الحسين، افتخار الدین البخاري (المولود في ٤٨٢هـ ، والمتوفى فى (٥٤٢هـ من كبار الفقهاء الحنفية في القرن السادس، وهو تلميذ قاضيخان وكتابه هذا كتاب مشهور معتمد في مجلد ذكر في أوله : "أنه كتب في هذا الفن خزانة الواقعات وكتاب النصاب، وسأل بعض إخوانه تلخيص نسخة يمكن ضبطها، فكتب الخلاصة جامع للرواية، خالية عن الزوائد تكتب الوان في السرح مع بيان مواضع المسائل وكتب فهرست الفصول والأحساس على رأس كل كتاب : ليكون عونا لمن ابتلى بالفتوى .. كذا في الكشف. وفيه تصريح يكون الخلاصة في مجلد مع أنه قد طبع في الهند في اربع مجلدات. وفى الكشف أيضا عند ذكر نصاب الفتيه أنه اختصر منه كتابه المسمى بخلاصة العناوي" . وقال مولانا عبد الحي في الفوائد أنه لخصه من الواقعات والخزانة ، فتدبر . واعلم أنه رحمه الله كان عديم النظير في ،زمانه فريد أئمة الدهر، شيخ الحنفية بما وراء النهر، ذكره المولى ابن كمال باشا الرومي من طبقة المجتهدين في المسائل الذين يقدرون على الاجتهاد في المسائل لا رواية فيها من صاحب المذهب، ولا يقدرون على مخالفته في الفروع والأصول. وله سوى الخلاصة تصانیف مقبولة منها : خزانة الفتاوى" و "خزانة الواقعات" ، و "نصاب الفقيه " . وأرخ صاحب الكشف وفاته عند ذكر تلك التصانيف سنة ٥٤٢هـ . فائدة : : ذكر صاحب البحر أن صاحب الخلاصة أعلم من صاحب الفتح أى ابن الهمام. وقال الشامي في حاشيته : يقال : إن الإمام المحقق له علم بالخلاف" .
40- Al-Khulasah: It is by al-Shaykh al-Imam Tahir bin Ahmad bin Abd al-Rashid bin al-Husayn, Iftikhar al-Din al-Bukhari (born in 482 AH, died in 542 AH). He was among the senior Hanafi jurists of the sixth century, and a student of Qadikhan. This book of his is a famous, relied-upon work in one volume. He mentioned in its beginning: 'He wrote in this field Khizanat al-Waqi'at and Kitab al-Nisab, and some of his brothers asked him for a summary that could be mastered, so he wrote al-Khulasah, comprehensive in narration, free from superfluous additions. Colors are written in the commentary with clarification of the places of masail, and he wrote an index of chapters and sections at the head of each book, to be a help for those who are afflicted with giving fatwa.' So it is in al-Kashf. And in it is an explicit statement that al-Khulasah is in one volume, although it has been printed in India in four volumes. And in al-Kashf also, when mentioning Nisab al-Futyah, that he abridged from it his book called Khulasat al-Anawi. And Mawlana Abd al-Hayy said in al-Fawa'id that he summarized it from al-Waqi'at and al-Khazanah, so reflect. And know that he, may Allah have mercy on him, was without peer in his time, unique among the imams of the age, the shaykh of the Hanafis in Transoxiana. Mawla Ibn Kamal Basha al-Rumi mentioned him among the class of mujtahids in matters [who are able to exert ijtihad in matters for which there is no narration from the founder of the school, but they cannot oppose him in furu' and usul]. Besides al-Khulasah, he has other accepted works, including: Khizanat al-Fatawa, Khizanat al-Waqi'at, and Nisab al-Fiqh. The author of al-Kashf dated his death when mentioning those works as 542 AH. Benefit: The author of al-Bahr mentioned that the author of al-Khulasah is more knowledgeable than the author of al-Fath, i.e. Ibn al-Humann. And al-Shami said in his gloss: 'It is said that the verifying imam had knowledge of ikhtilaf.'
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Imam Tahir al-Bukhari and his work al-Khulasah. It details his lineage, status as a mujtahid in masail, and his compilation method. Al-Khulasah is a relied-upon Hanafi fiqh manual that summarizes rulings from earlier works like Khizanat al-Waqi'at. The faida at the end notes a scholarly opinion that the author of al-Khulasah was more knowledgeable than Ibn al-Humann (author of Fath al-Qadir). This underscores the high regard for al-Khulasah in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
الخلاصة (al-Khulasah): A Hanafi fiqh compendium by Tahir al-Bukhari, summarizing rulings from Khizanat al-Waqi'at and other works, arranged with indices for easy reference.
مجتهد في المسائل (mujtahid fi al-masail): A jurist who can perform ijtihad for cases not directly narrated from the founder of the school (Abu Hanifa), but cannot contradict his usul and furu'.
خزانة الواقعات (Khizanat al-Waqi'at): One of the source works from which al-Khulasah was summarized; a collection of fatwa cases by Tahir al-Bukhari.
نصاب الفقه (Nisab al-Fiqh): Another source work by Tahir al-Bukhari, also summarized in al-Khulasah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was Tahir al-Bukhari's scholarly rank according to Ibn Kamal Basha?
A) Absolute mujtahid
B) Mujtahid fi al-masail
C) Muqallid mufti
D) Mujtahid fi al-ushul

Key Takeaway
Al-Khulasah is a highly authoritative Hanafi compendium by a mujtahid fi al-masail, designed with practical features for muftis.

Al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Its Author: A Cornerstone of Hanafi Fatwa
Biographical introduction to a key Hanafi fiqh text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and role of al-Durr al-Mukhtar in the Hanafi fatwa tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Durr al-Mukhtar by al-Haskafi is the authoritative Hanafi commentary relied upon for fatwa.

In this lesson, we explore al-Durr al-Mukhtar, a foundational text in Hanafi jurisprudence. Written by Muhammad Alauddin al-Haskafi, a mufti of Damascus, this commentary on Tanwir al-Absar became a primary source for issuing fatwas in the later Hanafi school. Understanding its author and significance is crucial for any student of Hanafi ifta'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book
Al-Durr al-Mukhtar is a commentary on the matn Tanwir al-Absar. Recognize that it is a sharh, not the original text.
This matn-commentary relationship is common in Hanafi literature.
2
Identify the author
The author is Muhammad Alauddin al-Haskafi. He held the position of mufti in Damascus and was a scholar of high repute, as shown by his teacher's praise.
His full lineage is given: son of the shaykh of the Umayyad Mosque.
3
Note the author's scholarly reputation
His shaykh, Muhammad Afandi, praised him for his virtue and thirst for knowledge, indicating his high standing among contemporaries.
Such ijazat (licenses) were common endorsements.
4
Recognize additional works
Al-Haskafi also wrote a more detailed commentary, Khaza'in al-Asrar wa Bada'i' al-Afkar fi Tanwir al-Absar. Its completion status is unknown.
This shows the author's dedication to explaining the same matn at different levels.
5
Understand the book's role in fatwa
Al-Durr al-Mukhtar is a key reference in Hanafi fatwa literature, often consulted alongside its commentary Radd al-Muhtar.
Later scholars like Ibn Abidin wrote super-commentaries on it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤١ - الدر المختار : هو شرح تنوير الأبصار للعلامة الفهامة محمد علاء الدين الحصكفى بن الشيخ على الإمام بجامع بني أمية ثم المفتى بدمشق المحمية، وهو صاحب التصانيف فى الفقه وغيره، قد أقر له بالفضل والتحقيق مشايخه وأهل عصره حتى قال شيخه العلامة محمد أفندى فى إجازته : " وإنه ممن نشأ والفضائل تعلّه وتنهله، والرغبة في العلم تقرب له ما يحاوله من ذلك وتسهله، حتى نال من قداح الكمال القدح المعلى، وفاز بما وشح به صدره وحلى . وللعلامة سوى هذا الشرح شرح آخر على نفس المتن باسم خزائن الأسرار وبدائع الأفكار في تنوير الأبصار" وهو شرح مبسوط، مفصل . والله أعلم هل كمله أم لا؟ وترجمه المحبى فى تاريخه فقال (ما مخلصه) : إنه
41- Al-Durr al-Mukhtar: It is a commentary on Tanwir al-Absar by the all-knowing, brilliant Muhammad Alauddin al-Haskafi, son of the shaykh and imam of the Umayyad Mosque, then mufti of protected Damascus. He is the author of works in fiqh and other disciplines. His shaykhs and contemporaries acknowledged his virtue and verification. His shaykh, the scholar Muhammad Afandi, said in his license: 'He is one who grew up with virtues nourishing him and a desire for knowledge making what he strives for easy and accessible, until he attained the highest mark of perfection and succeeded in adorning and beautifying his chest.' Besides this commentary, the scholar has another commentary on the same matn called Khaza'in al-Asrar wa Bada'i' al-Afkar fi Tanwir al-Absar, which is an extensive, detailed commentary. And Allah knows best whether he completed it or not. al-Muhibbi translated him in his history, saying (summary): 'He ...'
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage introduces al-Durr al-Mukhtar, the famous Hanafi fiqh commentary by Muhammad Alauddin al-Haskafi. It praises the author's erudition and mentions that he also wrote a more detailed commentary on the same text. The passage emphasizes the author's high standing among his contemporaries. This book is a cornerstone of Hanafi fatwa literature.

Key Terms
الدر المختار (al-Durr al-Mukhtar): A commentary on Tanwir al-Absar by al-Haskafi, a key Hanafi fiqh reference.
الحصكفى (al-Haskafi): Muhammad Alauddin al-Haskafi, the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
تنوير الأبصار (Tanwir al-Absar): The matn (base text) upon which al-Durr al-Mukhtar is a commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar?
A) Ibn Abidin
B) Muhammad Alauddin al-Haskafi
C) Ibn al-Humann
D) Tahir al-Bukhari

Key Takeaway
Al-Durr al-Mukhtar by al-Haskafi is a foundational commentary in Hanafi fiqh, relied upon for fatwa.
